O sons, since I have completed this book for you, which is the culmination of the medical science, with its conclusions, explanations, and clarifications, it seems to me that I have compiled this (book) for you along with this treatise, which is a part of the surgery branch of medicine, performed by hand.
For manual operation is prohibited in our region and time, and the knowledge of it has become very rare, and only a few small descriptions remain in the books of the ancients, which have been altered and corrupted so that their intentions are concealed, and the strength and art of it have been weakened.
And it seems to me that I should revive the method of this treatise through explanation, clarification, and abbreviation; and bring it with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools used in the work, along with additional explanations and preparations, which are necessary.
But the reason why no skilled craftsman is found with his hand in our time is that the art of medicine is extensive and requires its practitioner to be well-versed in the science of anatomy, which Galen describes as having knowledge of the limbs' assistance and forms, as well as their connection and separation. One must also have a understanding of bones, nerves, and tendons, along with their number and function, as well as the pulsating and non-pulsating veins, and the locations for their release.
And for this reason, Hippocrates says that a name is significant, but in the work it amounts to little, and even less so in the art of manual operation. (This quote emphasizes the importance of practical knowledge and skill over just theoretical or book learning.)
But we have already said this in the introduction of this book, for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy is not likely to avoid error, and because of that, many people die. Thus, I have seen many who are mistaken in this science and lack knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish and inexperienced doctor who attempted to lance an abscess on a woman's neck, cut some of her carotid arteries, causing massive bleeding, and the woman died in his hands. (This is a cautionary tale about the dangers of practicing medicine without proper knowledge and experience.)
And I saw another doctor who tried to remove a stone from a man's bladder while the patient was awake. The stone was large, and it came out along with a piece of his bladder. As a result, the man died three days later. (This is another cautionary tale about the risks of surgery.)
And I had already advised against it and saw that due to the size of the stone and the patient's condition, I knew that he would not survive. (This is a further illustration of the importance of proper medical judgment.)
And I saw another doctor who was paid by a duke in our land to perform surgery on a black castrated slave who had a fracture in his thigh. The ignorant doctor operated on the patient, setting the fracture with pillows and splints with excessive pressure, without allowing any ventilation of the wound. (This is an example of medical malpractice.)
And he bandaged him according to his own desires and left the wound unattended for several days, ordering that it not be opened or cared for. As a result, both the patient's thigh and foot became infected, leading to gangrene and ultimately death. (This is an example of medical neglect.)
I was called to the patient and prepared to unbind the wound. Once I did so, the patient found relief from his pain and regained some composure. (This is an example of proper medical care.)
However, the infection had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not stop it from spreading further. The patient's condition worsened as the infection continued to spread throughout his body. (This is an example of a severe medical emergency.)
And I saw another doctor who lanced a cancerous abscess and it became infected for several days, worsening the patient's condition significantly. (This is an example of improper medical treatment.)
The reason for this is that the cancerous growth is caused by black bile, and therefore should not be treated with cauterization in all cases, but rather in a location where it can coexist with the rest of the body. (This is an example of medical reasoning.)
Therefore, sons, it is necessary for you to distinguish between two types of manual operation: those associated with health and wellness, and those involving risk or danger in more complex cases. (This is an example of medical judgment.)
I have already discussed in every part of this book the operation that involves error and fear; therefore, it is essential for you to be mindful of this and avoid it, so that you are not misled by false information or deception. (This is an example of medical caution.)
Therefore, take up your weapons (your medical skills) with diligence and under the protection of God, and approach your patients with ease and confidence. (This is an example of medical encouragement.)
And use the best method to bring about health and praiseworthy success through God's grace, and leave behind the terrible diseases that are difficult to cure. Set aside your fears and hesitations in your faith and name, for it is more glorious for you to remain steadfast, both now and forever, as a testament to your sanctity. (This is an example of medical advice and encouragement.)
Galen also said in some of his monitions: "Do not treat a bad illness with poor medical skills, lest you be known as a bad doctor." (This is an example of medical ethics.)

And I say that cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm caused by the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of what is attracted with cautery, and especially if the cautery is for necessary pains or painful necessities, strong and intense, which do not tolerate delay, due to fear of those who bring malice, which is greater than any small harm that may enter through the time.

And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this without reason, but rather because of the equality of gold and the loftiness of its substance.
And they said that the location of cautery does not matter, but this is not absolutely true, as I have proven and discovered that it only works in some bodies without others, and cauterization with this is good and better than iron as they said; but when you perform cautery with fire and gold, it is not so simple, because the gold ignites according to the amount of heat you want due to its brightness, and it prepares to receive the treatment; and if you place a flame on top of it, the gold will melt in the fire, and some layers will be burnt due to the intensity of the craftsman's work.
And therefore, cautery is performed with iron more lightly and more directly according to the operation.

On cauterization of water that descends in the groin.

Chapter 16.
On the cautery for the eyelid of the eye when the hair has turned inward and is causing pain to the eye.
When the eyelashes have turned inward and are causing pain to the eye, there are two ways to cauterize: one is with fire, and the other is with a burning medicine.
If using a cautery of fire, command the patient to read his eyelashes as if he were cleaning them, extending and moistening them; and if it is painful, then you strengthen the patient's eyes with a bandage around them until the lashes grow back.

And let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of the body part, and let the cauteries be according to the length of the straight body part.
And do not press too hard with the cautery.
And if the amount of fluid that has accumulated is equal to the size of the affected area of the kidney, and if it is not any more than that; and if the patient is standing on their feet; and if they are not standing, then have them lie down, with their limbs extended and their arms raised.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a scalpel, when you have skill and prudence in the art.
And be careful not to overdo it in the cauterization, and let the entire kidney be cauterized so that all of the body is affected and it reaches into the intestines, for here the kidney is delicate; and know this.
Chapter 28.
Of the perforation of an abscess in the liver with a cautery.
When a tumor or abscess forms in the liver and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in its membrane, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient will suffer from heaviness and dull pain without acute symptoms.
And if it is in the membrane of the liver, with great and often exhausting pain for doctors during treatment.
Therefore it is necessary for the patient to be positioned face down on their chest, and gently touch the location of the abscess with a finger; then heat the cautery that has been prepared in the shape of a scalpel, as shown on the previous page. And cauterize with that cautery until the entire kidney is compressed, until it reaches the bladder, and until pus forms.
And treat that perforation with the same care as for other abscesses until it is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this form of cautery unless you have extensive training in the medical art and have learned about many illnesses; but try this method a few times with caution on this operation, yet leave it to those who know better, and that is best.
Chapter 29.
On the cauterization of wounds or ulcers.
The ancients used to cauterize wounds or ulcers by shaping them according to this method: take a dry reed from the stalks of Aristolochia, and shape it into a long, pointed instrument as thick as your finger.
And then submerge that in oil and heat it over a flame, and then cauterize with a pointed instrument at the location between the continuation of the collarbone and the neck; and with two small instruments place them below, slightly declining towards the area beneath the chin, and with two others on the sides where they decline between the fifth rib and the waist, declining slightly towards the back; and with another on the middle of the chest; and one more above the stomach, and three on the back; and with one at the location between the shoulder blades, and with two on either side of the lower back, below the instrument that is between the shoulder blades.
And do not press too hard with the cautery, but rather let it gently touch the surface of the kidney.
And some ancient physicians, who were men, would use a cautery made of iron that was shaped like a ray and heat it before placing it on the location between the ribs, allowing it to reach the abscess and expel pus, just as we mentioned for liver abscesses.
But in this perforation with cautery, there is fear, for one may die or suffer an accident in the wound that will not heal.
Chapter 30.
On the cauterization of the spleen.
When you treat the illness of the spleen with what we have said about treatment in division and do not combine your treatments, then there are three methods for cauterizing it, all of which are appropriate, one of which is to make three or four small incisions along the length of the spleen, according to the shape of the cauteries for the liver, as shown on the preceding page.
And let the thickness between each cautery be that of a finger or slightly more, and the method for cauterizing should be the same as we described for liver cauteries.
And do not press too hard with the cauteries, and let the patients be on their right side.
And there is another method for cauterization, which involves heating the cautery with two twists, causing heat that we mentioned in the chapter on dislocation of the muscle, and lifting the kidney that is located at the end of the spleen where it lies on the left side of the patient.
And let your elevation be the same as the length of the body, so that the cauteries are made according to the width of the trunk.
And then insert the two twists and heat them slightly, causing penetration into the kidney from the other side.
And then extract the cauteries, resulting in four incisions.
And if you wish, cauterize with a three-twist cautery.
And then you should treat the cauteries to ensure that they have not remained too long without being cleaned, as this is more conducive to healing than previous causes.
Chapter 31.
On the cauterization of dropsy.
Cautery is not used in cases of dropsy, except in specific instances.
When treating dropsy with the methods of treatment that we have discussed in division and you do not combine your treatments, then it is necessary to cauterize with four incisions around the belly button and one above the stomach, another above the liver, another above the spleen, two between the vertebrae of the back, one on the right side of the chest, and another above the stomach. And the depth of the incision made by the cautery should be proportionate to the thickness of the kidney.
And then let the cauteries remain open for some time to allow for drainage.
And do not quickly remove patients from treatment after cautery, for it is necessary to add two intentions and wait some time for healing to occur.
The shape of the cautery used to burn the belly should be like the one described previously, and is the one that is used to burn the back and is shaped like an olive, as described in its form before.
Chapter thirty-two.
On the cauterization of the feet and thighs.
When the feet are swollen with dropsy and filled with serous water, it is necessary to cauterize the feet on the back of the foot in the space between the auricular (outer ankle) and the ring finger (heel), and raise your hand with the cautery without twisting it; and then lift your hand without returning it completely, because the serous water will evaporate.
The cautery should be in the following shape: And make two cauteries on both thighs, and on each thigh make a pointed cautery with the tip of the scalpel-shaped cautery. And let the cautery be the length of the thigh, and place one below the knee and the other just above the middle of the thigh, and on each thigh two cauteries.
And leave the wound open for a long time after treatment so that some water may drain from it.
And treat it with those causes that we have mentioned.
Chapter thirty-three.
On the cauterization of the belly.
When the belly is weak and humid to the point of weakening its virtues, that is, the digestive and retentive virtues which are in the stomach and intestines, it is cured with methods of treatment and not compared; and sometimes the patient endures a cautery that expels the virtue, therefore cauterize the belly with a large cautery on the stomach as preceded in the cauterization of the stomach, with a circular cautery and four subtle cauteries around the navel, with a fine pointed cautery; and with a cautery on the bladder over the renal region, or two cauteries.
And if sometimes the humors are excessive and the patient tolerates it, therefore cauterize above the navel and on the intestines, and lightly adjust two cauteries on the stomach and near the inguinal regions, because this is a perfect treatment and you will not err with its help.
Chapter thirty-four.
On the cauterization of old hemorrhoids.
When hemorrhoids are of a gross nature or are caused by corrupted humors or moisture, and have been treated as previously mentioned and do not respond to that treatment, then cauterize with three cauteries on the pus below the small and small triangular spine, and with a cautery above the navel that passes through two ditches.
And if you think that his stomach is cold and the food is not digested, and the face appears swollen, therefore cauterize the stomach with a large cautery as previously described; and with one cautery on the spleen, and with another cautery on the liver of the patient with a pointed cautery, and leave the cautery open for some time to drain, and treat him until he is healed.
Chapter thirty-five.
Chapter thirty-five: On the cauterization of abscesses and their surgical removal.
When you surgically remove an abscess, then you should cauterize the wound with a pointed cautery that resembles a ray. After introducing the cautery into the cavity of the abscess, then place your finger over the cautery and move it towards the opening of the vein from which the blood flows.
And do this once or twice, because if there are many abscesses, then cauterize each of them as we have said, and treat those with ointments until they are healed.
And if you cauterize with a large cautery on a swelling, it is more beneficial.
Chapter thirty-six.
Chapter thirty-six: On the cauterization of fistulas that are formed in the lower parts of the body.
If nature does not obey the treatment that we have recommended in its place and the patient is frightened by this, let him be healed with cautery.
Therefore, when you find a fistula in the lower parts of the body that is old and has become corrupted with pus and moisture, it is fitting that you probe it with a slender instrument and determine its depth with the previously mentioned probe.
And apply the cautery, which is similar to a ray. And then introduce the heated cautery into this fistula, and according to the depth that you have measured with the probe.
And iterate the application of the cautery on that area until the corrupt flesh is completely burned, one or two or three times, according to the degree of your necessity.
And beware of burning of nerve and vein; or if a fistula goes to the bladder's body or the hernia's body, then beware of all those areas; and do not do that unless the fistula is in a fleshy location and you think it is not penetrating.
Then heal the wound in that area until it is healed.
And if the wound is sealed and the pus is drained from it and remains like that for a long time, then know that it is completely healed.[It seems that this medieval medical treatise is providing instructions on how to care for wounds, specifically in cases where there may be joint pain caused by cold humors. The text suggests using cautery on the foot if necessary, returning intestines or hernias to their proper place, and being careful not to burn nerves or veins when treating a wound. It also notes that a sealed wound with drained pus that remains for a long time is a sign of complete healing.]
And if the matter is not easily drained, then know that it is penetrating or in the marrow of the bone and is corrupt, or this is caused by one of those things which will be mentioned in its place.

And use light cauterization with the second one a little less, so that three linear cauteries will come, and then they will serve more in aid.

Of cauterization of bladder.
When a weakness and softening occurs in the bladder due to cold and moisture, so that the patient cannot retain urine, then cauterize that area with a pointed cautery below the navel, where the skin of the pubis begins, and cauterize on one side with a cautery, and on the other side as well.
And let the length of each cautery be according to the amount of nodes in the swelling; and cauterize that with a cautery at the lowest part of the back, or with two cauteries if necessary.
And let the cautery be pointed according to what is prescribed.
Chapter 39.[This could be the beginning of a new section or chapter in the medical treatise. Without more context it is difficult to say for certain what this chapter might cover.]
Of cauterization of the uterus.
When there is cold and moisture in the uterus, and for this reason conception is prohibited, and menstruation is corrupted, and its onset is delayed, and pain occurs during their occurrence, then it is necessary that the area be cauterized with three cauteries along the navel circumference, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder; and with a pointed cautery on the area below the back, or with two cauteries, and let the cauteries be pointed.

Of cauterization of dislocation of the ankle.
When moisture and swelling have infiltrated the area of the ankle, and are causing fluid to accumulate in that location, and a sign of this is that one thigh is longer than the other when compared, then it is necessary to cauterize that area with a pointed cautery. And the location of the dislocation is found in that place where it protrudes.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the patient on the area of the ankle with a circular-shaped cautery, since you will have marked it with a probe in the circumference of that area as it is turned, and so that the affected area falls in the middle of the circle.
And let the cautery be in the form of the one prescribed for stomach cauterization.
And if this cautery is not available to you, then cauterize that area with three large olive-shaped cauteries.
And let the cauteries be made according to the thickness of the entire spine; and then heal that area until it is healed.
Chapter 41.[This could be the beginning of a new section or chapter in the medical treatise. Without more context it is difficult to say for certain what this chapter might cover.] [Continued in next message due to character limit] [Starting the next message]
Of cauterization of the sciatic vein.
When pain occurs in the area of the ankle, and is caused by cold and moisture, the patient can be treated with what we have said, but that is outdated. Therefore, it is necessary to purge the patient of thick humors with foul-smelling pills or artificial pills, and then cauterize that area.
And the method of cauterization in this case is according to two methods: either cauterization with burning medicines, or cauterization with fire.
It is done according to two scientific methods, one of which is that you cauterize that on the area of the ankle with three triangular-shaped cauteries in this form; and do so with good depth. And let the spaces between each cautery be the width of a finger, and if the cauteries are olive-shaped or large.
Surgeons should make four cauterizations on the same spot above the ankle.
And if desired, cauterize using the ring that precedes the shape in the cauterization of the ankle dislocation, making sure the circle is continuous and burns the surface of the entire tendon.
And this is the method for cauterization in sciatica, when pain is adhered to the ankle and not extended into the thigh.
But if it extends into the thigh, then cauterize with two cauterizations on the thigh at the point where the pain is located, and with one cauterization on the ankle for four times a little above the inner part.
And if using a scalpel-like cautery, then adjust the depth of the cautery according to the thickness of the tendon's surface.
And if the patient points to a location near the toes as where the pain is located, then cauterize that area with three or four points using the cautery, or more if necessary.
And if the patient points to pain below the groin towards the thigh, then cauterize that area with a scalpel-like cautery.
And be careful during all cauterization that you do not burn the nerves or large artery with the cautery, as this can cause further harm or spasm to the patient.
And I have seen some who, while cauterizing above the ankle, burned too much during the procedure, and the leg became swollen with inflammation all the way to the foot, and it became perforated and corrupt throughout the foot. Chapter 42.
Chapter 42: On the Cauterization of Pain in Two Places.
Sometimes pain can occur in two places due to various causes, such as impact or trauma, excessive evacuation, or other similar factors. Pain can also be caused by the infusion of wet and cold substances into the body.
And cautery should only be used in this one case, which is made for the effusion of matter. (or the removal of matter through burning)
Therefore, it is appropriate to evacuate the patient with purged pills that resemble theirs, which should be made on the side where the pain is, three lines according to its latitude (width). Then make an incision or larger cauterization on each line, depending on the amount of tolerance of the patient and their strength.

Chapter 43.
On cauterization at the beginning of abscess (or boil).
Many times this illness affects small children, and the sign of its beginning in children is that it occurs on their forehead, above their eyebrows, causing an elevation and movement.
And you will find it in the last lumbar vertebra of the back, and the knots of it that already begin to rise above the other vertebrae.
And therefore when you see this and wish to prevent it, then cauterize that area with a circular cautery in the following form: so that the cautery takes in all parts of the vertebra equally.
And if you wish, cauterize around the circumference of the vertebra with a pointed cautery two or three lines. And let the points be close to each other.
Then heal the area until it is healed with what we have mentioned before. (presumably rest, cleanliness and proper dressing of the wound)
But be careful not to apply cautery in abscess that is caused by nerve spasm.
Chapter 44.
On cauterization for gout (or foot joint pain) and joint pain.
When joint pain is caused by cold humors that infiltrate each part of the body, and pain occurs in the feet, it is customarily called gout by doctors.
And therefore, when gout caused by cold humor is cured with treatment and the pain is not relieved, then relieve it with cauterization.
And you should cauterize that area to promote evacuation around the circumference of the joint of the foot with multiple cauteries.
And let the cautery be olive-shaped, like this: (presumably a description or depiction of an olive-shaped cautery is provided here but not included in the text)
And if it is necessary to make points on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. And if the pain rises into the toes or other joints and this happens often, then cauterize that area around each toe with three or four cauteries on all sides using the olive-shaped cautery. [I'm assuming the text refers to "toes" when it mentions "denolhs", as "denolh" could be translated as nail but that doesn't make much sense in this context]
And if many cauteries are necessary, then cauterize that area and do not press too hard with the cautery beforehand, but rather only roughly trace the outline of the cautery. (or only make a light touch)
And if the pain rises into the toe and foot, then administer the cautery as we have mentioned in its chapter. (presumably referring to a previously described method for cauterizing the foot)
And if the pain is only in the hands and it is called sugar (or diabetes), then make pricks around the circumference of the fingers as they bend, prick two lines. (or prick two rows)
And if pain remains in the fingers mentioned before, then prick around the circumference of each finger and at the base of the thumb.
And if the pain rises after several days to the knees or the muscles, then cauterize each of them on all sides at the points where they need help. (presumably referring to areas that are identified as particularly painful or swollen)
And you will not evacuate the patient with good self-care and reception of medications, because if good self-care is followed and inflammation is evacuated with this cautery, then it will heal, God willing.
Chapter 45.
On cauterization for ruptures (or tears in the flesh or muscle).
When there is a rupture in the groin, with intestines protruding before the hernia in the genital area and it begins to spread, then it is necessary for the patient to refrain from eating on that day and use laxatives so that the incision made by the hernia in their belly closes. [Note: The text seems to be talking about an inguinal hernia that has become strangulated and needs to be treated with cautionery, but it is not clear how this relates to the previous sentence]
And keep the patient between your hands on their back, and command them to hold their stomach inside so that no blood or hernia or intestines appear.
And return that area to its previous state with your hands, and make an incision or mark the rupture on the bone of the pelvis with a sign that resembles the top of a circle at the highest parts of the body. (presumably referring to the iliac crest)

until it becomes very red and throws sparks. (or glowing embers) Then return the intestine or hernia to its cavity, and place your hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out. (presumably while cauterizing)

Then place the cautery on that mark with your hand, holding the cautery perpendicularly, and direct it towards the bone of the pelvis in the middle of the incision; and repeat this again if you have not achieved success in the first attempt at reaching the bone.
And observe carefully the location of the intestine during your cauterization, so that you do not burn it and cause injury or great harm to the patient.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, then your operation is not successful.
And it is necessary for a child's cautery to be fine according to their age and size. (presumably referring to the size or shape of the cautery)

Chapter 53
Of cauterization of boils and similar things
Many times the lower parts of a sick person's feet become affected by a disease called a boil (clau), which is a large, open wound that causes lameness. Cauterization in these cases can be done in two ways: with fire or with hot water.
However, cauterization with fire is done by heating the concave cautery, similar in shape to a vulture's beak, made of iron and sized according to the size of the entire boil, and with fine edges.
And then place the hot cautery on top of the boil and rotate your hand with the cautery around the boil until the cautery reaches the depth of the boil. And leave it alone for three days until it begins to ooze pus. And then apply a plaster made of crushed mallow leaves, salt and leave it on for one night because that will help to draw out any remaining pus or infection from the wound.
And then you should treat the area with a meat-generating ointment until it is healed.
And if they are not converted (to healthy tissue), and many times this happens on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet, then it is necessary to use cauterization with water, by taking a small amount of iron or steel or vulture's beak and placing it over the boil; and then let a little bit of hot water flow into the small cup of the tool, and keep your hand steady, and you rotate the tool with pressure from your entire hand, and press the edge of the tool into the root of the boil, and find the path for the hot water to reach the core of the boil; and then let the patient endure the biting sensation of the hot water for an hour, and then remove it, because the boil with its roots will be eradicated.
And do this for those lying down, and bring the other one over so that it covers all of them, which are outside their bodies.
Then treat the pus from wounds caused by nail extractions with remedies that help the flesh grow back together, using ointments.
Chapter III
On the Cautery Treatment of Tremors.
When you encounter a tremor due to cold in the nerves or fever from an unknown cause, or for any similar reason, it is necessary that you apply four or five cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and another cautery on the soles of the feet, and a round-shaped "olivar" cautery over the stomach.
And the trembling will subside, thus hastening the recovery from the cold-related illness.
Chapter LV
On the Cautery Treatment of Symptoms related to Whiteness in the Body.
When there is whiteness in the body and pustules with cracks that are formed by thick, corrupted materials, it is necessary at first, as a preliminary measure, to cauterize the top of the fistula with a thin, pointed cautery made from myrtle wood, with its tip extended using fire; or with long-bladed surgical knives; or with lenticular cauteries.
Some veins also need to be cauterized initially at the beginning of their expulsion according to this method; they do not bleed and have an excess that needs removal, so they are broken open and healed from it.
However, it is necessary to do this through evacuation by using phlebotomy (bloodletting).
Chapter LVI
On the Cautery Treatment of Swelling from a Ruptured Vessel through Incision of the Artery.
When you encounter swelling from a ruptured vessel that is treated with an incision in the affected area, which is often on the outside or at the site of abscesses or cauterization of the limb, it is difficult to heal this condition.
Therefore, when this occurs, you should place your hand over the orifice of the vein and hold it there; press on the area with your fingers to restrict the flow of blood from the affected area and prevent further issues.
Then place the large, round-shaped cauteries over the fire and hold them there until they become quite hot, blowing on them so that they are well heated.
Then take one of the hot cauteries, either small or large, depending on the location and severity of the ruptured artery, and place it immediately over the vein that is causing the blood flow; hold it there until the area becomes cauterized and the bleeding stops.
And if the blood is still flowing from the orifice of the artery when you apply pressure with the cautery, take another hot cautery from those prepared in the fire and immediately place it over the area; do not stop doing this until the bleeding has stopped completely.
And make sure not to burn the nerves, which could lead to further complications for the patient.
And you should know that when blood flows from an artery, it is impossible to stop the bleeding in those cases, especially when the artery is large, without one of four methods: using cautery as described earlier; through extraction when not already extracted, as extracting its ends causes them to burn and constricts the blood flow; tying it with strong ligatures made from bile or lime; placing medicines over it that have the power to restrict blood flow, and strengthened by a bolster and proper binding.
However, the one who administers binding with lime and strong ligatures using cloth or hot compresses should not be too confident, as this method is questionable.
However, if this occurs in someone's presence without a doctor or medicine available, then use gentle pressure with your finger on the orifice of the vein as we have described before, and focus on the tight binding of it until the bleeding stops completely from the top part of the wound. Do not apply pressure to the artery. Additionally, sprinkle cold water over the artery so that the blood becomes congealed and thicker; then consider whether cautery or medicine is necessary.

Capital III.
On extracting (removing) the temporal arteries.

Chapter VII.
Of the cure for blockage of ears.
Sometimes newborns get blockage in their ears from the wombs of their mothers, which has not been pierced, and this can also happen to adults, due to earwax or flesh growing inside the ear; and sometimes this blockage occurs in the entrance of the ear canal, which is not noticeable, and sometimes it happens in the outer parts.
And the one that occurs in the entrance of the ear canal, which is not noticeable, is among the most difficult cases to cure.
And in the case where you can see the blockage, it is necessary to expose the patient's ear to the sun and observe it. And so if you see a visible blockage, open it with a thin spatula, of which this is the shape:
Let the tip of it be small in width, with one side being sharp and the other not, and let the spatula be two finger-widths wide so that it does not harm the ear.
And so if the blockage is due to flesh grown inside the ear or its canal, then use thin forceps and carefully cut the flesh until all of it is removed.
And if the blockage is in the entrance of the ear canal, then take a thin rod, heat it slightly over fire, and gently insert it into the ear canal.
And so if you have noticed blockage with what the patient finds difficult to hear, gently relieve the pressure, and make sure not to harm the nerves of the ear.
And then place a cloth on the ear according to the size of the opening you have created and wrapped with Egyptian wax; do this for several days until you are sure that the wound has healed; or take some herb, soak it in water, grind it into powder, and apply it three times a day; and if you see that the ear has become inflamed, then you must lance it and replace the dressing with another one wrapped in wax made from roasted oil, until the swelling subsides; and continue to treat it until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs, then submerge a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear, and use the other treatment that stops the flow of blood, which is called "distillation" in the treatise.
Chapter VIII.
On the treatment of blepharitis, which occurs on the eyelids.
Blepharitis, which sometimes occurs due to excess moisture and sometimes dryness in the eyes.
Therefore, it is necessary to have tweezers or forceps and cut the eyelashes with their roots using a spatula, and then place them on the affected area three times a day.
But if pain and bleeding occur, then cauterize it using a pointed ocular cautery.
And the best cauterization is to treat the incisions and wounds multiple times until there is no longer any cause for their roots to grow back, and when they are cauterized with fire, their roots are burned and do not return.

Treatment for styes that occur on the eyelids. [https://www.poemhunter.com/poems/the-divine-comedy-inferno-canto-1/](https://www.poemhunter.com/poems/the-divine-comedy-inferno-canto-1/)
Often, small bumps occur on the eyelids that are similar to styes in their firmness and hardness, and because of this similarity, they are also called "grandissia".
And it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the eyelid, both above and below.
Therefore, the operation for this condition is to first determine if the "grandissia" protrudes from the eyelid and is swollen on all sides, and if the cause of it is minor.
Therefore, make an incision on it with a scalpel along its width, and then carefully cauterize all around until it dries up, and then use forceps to lift and cut it off.
And if the bump is large, then adjust it with stitches and treat it until it heals.
But if it is small, you will not encounter any problems because the ointment used for treatment will restore and heal it.
If the bump is protruding towards the inner parts of the eyelid, then expose the eyelid and lift the bump using forceps, making sure to avoid any unnecessary incisions. Press it gently from all sides, and if an incision on the eyelid is required, make it carefully. However, if the eyelid incision is long, this should not be a concern.
And then make an incision, rinse the eye with salt water, and treat the area with an ointment that promotes healing until it is cured.
Chapter X. [https://www.poemhunter.com/poems/the-divine-comedy-inferno-canto-1/](https://www.poemhunter.com/poems/the-divine-comedy-inferno-canto-1/)
Of the treatment of abscess above the eye.
An abscess is an injury that forms in the tunic of the upper eyelid, and it often affects children, causing them discomfort and redness and impeding their vision; as a result, tears gather in their eyes and they cannot look at the brightness of the sun.
And so the children rub their eyes constantly and even sleep on them, and the eyelashes of their lower eyelids are damp, indicating an imminent abscess; moreover, when you press on the area with your fingers, you can feel it swell up inside.
One method of treatment for this condition involves the patient placing their head over your thigh and covering themselves with a cloth to keep warm; then, you should make a circle of appropriate size around the swelling, using a bandage that covers all areas affected by abscess, and place it on top of the area while applying pressure with your fingers to promote the gathering of pus in the center of the circle. Then, create an incision in the middle of the swelling with a scalpel or similar instrument, making sure the cut is no wider than that made during bloodletting.
However, it is important that you make the incision deep enough to reach the pus, as in severe cases, pus may spread through the swelling, requiring a wider opening similar to that made during an incision for whitlow.
Therefore, remove the pus using cloths that you had placed on top of the incision, turning them over and over with your right and left hands until they are saturated with it.
And make sure not to touch the incision with your fingers, to prevent accidental contact with the eye or causing any damage.
But if you don't see any pus at the start of the incision, you can insert a probe into the opening until it reaches the abscess; then remove the pus as previously described. Afterwards, place damp cloths soaked in wine and vinegar over the area, and secure them with bandages.
Also, for ulcers that produce excessive discharge, apply salt in the cavity of the incision to absorb any remaining moisture.
And take care of it until it heals completely.
But if an abscess forms in the same area, you should treat it with a plaster made of powdered galls until it heals completely.
Chapter 11.
Chapter 11: Methods of eye examination.
When eyelashes grow abnormally and become ingrown, causing discomfort and leading to various eye conditions such as chronic tearing, swelling of the eyelids, and clouding of the cornea that is referred to as tactinir of the eye, it can be treated in four ways: using a hot cautery; applying a sharp medicine as previously mentioned in the chapter on cauterization; performing an incision and stitching it up; or using rods as I will explain.
And so it is necessary that you place the patient's head on your lap; then turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand, and if it is turned, good; and if not, insert a needle in the one where there is more swelling below the eyelid, and make the needle with pus penetrate near the edge of the eyelid where hairs grow, and pull the pus upwards with the eyelid, and turn it with the rod.
And then make an incision in the inner part of the eyelid below the hairs, using a sharp spatula from the lacrimal major to the lacrimal minor; and then extract the pus and place it beneath the eyelid, sprinkling fine particles of linen or cloth, and then cover the eyelid with a compress, and let it be in the shape of a myrtle leaf.
However, it is necessary that the shape be according to the degree of swelling of the eyelid, because this varies in people, for there are some who require a large incision in the eyelid according to the degree of swelling, as the eyelid becomes softened.
And then make an incision with the spatula along the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the lacrimal major and end at the lacrimal minor. And if your incision is near the natural hairs, as thick as a king's beard.
And then place the ounce in one of the two angles of the eyelid, and then scrape it all, and then attach with the incision the two lips with subtle wool or lamb's gall, and clean the blood, and if you want to do so, stick what is superfluous from the pus on two eyebrows with some sticking causes, and if not, don't worry about it.
And then leave the suture of the wounds for three or four days, and take care of it.
And if you want, leave the wound without sutures and take care of it with what dries and constricts, because the eyelid is swollen due to the seal of the wound and its accumulation; but a suture is better. Therefore, I say this in contrast to old beliefs.
But still, it is advisable to pay attention to the patient and do a good job, not out of fear.
And there is another way to suture, which is to place on the eyelid a shape like a myrtle leaf, and then raise the eyelid with three separate and joined hooks according to this form:
But if that is not possible, take the hooks and place them so that they are not wet, then take a needle with thread and insert it in the middle of the shape, and insert one pus near the lacrimal major and the other near the lacrimal minor, and adjust between your fingers the threads evenly, and then raise your hand with equal elevation, raise the entire eyelid over which the mark has been made as we have recommended.
And then adjust the two lips of the wound with a suture, and take care of it until it heals.
But if an abscess occurs at your incision or cut, calm it with wax and similar things, and with ointments.
And sometimes the hairs of the eyelid turn inward, so it is necessary to use what we have said about incisions, but a suture is more artificial in each case.
To cure with canes is according to this form: and it is to turn the eyelid and cut the shape that is inside as I have told you; and then for art, make two canes or two thin rods whose length is according to the length of the eyelid and the width of them is smaller than the width of the spatula. And you have already incised at the ends of each part, where there are threads.
And then add each one with subtlety on top of what is superfluous from the eyelid and the eye, and tighten the canes of each part with strong pressure, and leave it for a few days, because the eyelid will die and become darkened due to the pressure and swell inside until it falls by itself.
But if it takes too long, then break it with the rods, and then take care of the wound until it heals.
And so when it is solidified, the eyelid is raised and the hairs do not hurt.
And this is the form of two rods that you will make according to this form: and it should have the quantity of length and width neither more nor less.
Chapter XII.
About raising the painful hairs in the eye with a needle when the hair is hard.
When they are not natural hairs, hard, rough and painful in the eyes, then the operation is to take a thin needle and place it in fine wax of cedar and lion, and then adjust the ends of it carefully and tie each one with great subtlety. And let the length of the threads be the quantity of one palm.
And then you make another fine thread below it in a short time, and tie the ends of it if you wish.
And then have the patient place their head in your lap, and let it be near the sun so that your work is visible, because it is a subtle and small operation.
And then insert the needle in the root of the hair that is attached and requires skill, and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid until you extract it above the natural hair.
And then pull the hair upwards and insert that into an incision, and let there be one or two or three hairs and not more.
And then pull your hand with that until the hair is extracted from the eyelid with an incision in the eyelid along with the natural hair.
But if it is pulled with an incision and the hair is not extracted, pull the incision towards the bottom with the wax that you have made with that, until the incision of the upper part is removed.
And look at that with the vision of the eye, because then you will remove the incision and the wax, and close each one and bandage the eye, and leave it for two or three days until the hair adheres to its place and grows well on top of it.
And if the hair is shorter than natural, then adjust a long hair from the natural hairs and raise it with that or leave it inside until it grows longer over some distance, and then you raise it.
Chapter XIII.
About the treatment of hematoma that comes to the eyelid above.
When hematoma comes to the eye and is a contraction of the eyelid when it contracts upwards, or to the right or left side, due to poor consolidation of wounds or sections or cauterization, and it is called "leporina", and this hematoma is natural or accidental, and is caused by consolidation of wounds or sections or cauterization, or similar to their malpractice.
But the way of operating in it is that you cut the consolidation and separate its lips, and place in it something made of linen cloth, and tie those together until they are healed.
And it is not necessary to use a cure for that from the causes that dry and constrict, because if you do so, the hematoma will return worse than ever before.
Use in it causes that soften, such as fenugreek, and cook it with water in which althea and fenugreek seeds have been boiled, or ointment of diacilion, which is liquefied with one of the oils, and submerge in it the linen cloth, and heal with that.
And the treasure of your cure is to penetrate with all skill that it is not consolidated according to the form that was at the beginning.
And this operation that we have said is nothing but a rectification of hematoma that does not return the form of the place to what it was before.
Chapter XIV.
About the treatment of hematoma that is made in the eyelid below.
This ophthalmia which is made in the lower eyelid, which is truly called ophthalmia; and it is some natural, others accidental.
Accidental [one] is made by plague, or by cut, or by cautery, or by similar things.
And the method of the operation for it is that you take a needle with double thread, and insert that in the flesh, and make it pass from the lacrimal of left to the lacrimal of right, so that the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.
And then stretch the flesh towards the parts above with the needle and cut it with the needle, and make an incision wide with a spatula. And so, if the shape of the eyelid returns as it should, that is good; and if not, take the thread and place it in the split shape, and with that turn the eyelid, and make the two cuts on the edge of the lower eyelid.
And let the ends of the two cuts be at two corners of the incision, which you have made where they converge, and let it be an angle of their making where, when they come together, a figure is made.
And this figure is the Greek letter: lambda.
And then remove the flesh from there by the amount that is the edge of the sharp lower part of it, so that the eyelid is cut.
And then adjust the separated parts and sew them together with wool thread; and then cure it with what we have said of the softening medicines and of the cauterization until it is healed.
And if the ophthalmia develops through a fissure or stitch or cautery, then it is necessary to make a flat cut with a fissure over the skin of the eyelid as described above. And then separate with the cauterization between two lips as we have said.
In summary of the discussion on the treatment of ophthalmia above or below, let it flow in the operation as prepared according to the form of the ophthalmia, and that is in the shape of diverse swellings.
And the wise artisans always prepare in every way that is possible for them to restore the shape to its natural form, or close to it, and the patient according to what is suitable for him from the operation and the instruments in the best dispositions.
Chapter 15.
Chapter 15: On the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva or to the cornea.
When this adhesion occurs in many people such that the eyelid is solidified over the white of the eye and it is prevented from moving easily and performing its natural functions, then it is necessary to insert the end of the thread under the eyelid, and raise it or stretch it with a hook.
And then you make an incision in the adhesion with a thin spatula, which does not have sharp edges from the cuts, so that the patient is not disturbed by the operation, and leave the spatula in place so as not to damage the eye with its sharpness.
And let your incision be such that it removes the adhesion easily until the eyelid has returned to its natural shape and the entire adhesion is healed.
And then you put salt water in the eye, which you use to rinse it; or distill juniper dissolved in water on it.
And then separate the eyelid from the eye with a cautery of fig tree, and place on the eye wool soaked in egg white, and for the third day use consolidating causes until it is healed.

Chapter 16: On the incision of a nail and the prominence of flesh around the tear ducts.
Know that a nail can be of two types: either it is nervous, and it resembles hard dry cypress; or it is not nervous, resembling white congealed moisture, which when touched with iron, can easily be lifted with a hook, and the hook does not penetrate into it.
And with both types, the condition does not begin until it reaches the inner part of the tear duct and gradually covers the eye, preventing light and movement of the eyelid.
But the method of working in the incision of it is that the patient puts his head back, and then you open the eyes and lift the eyelid with your hand, and then gather the nail with a hook with doubled thickness and stretch it upwards to the sides. And then take a needle and insert in it a horsehair or ox or cow hair, or similar, or strong bile, or double the tip of the needle little by little and put that in the middle of the nail, and insert it with the needle, and bind the nail with bile; and extend that to the cuticles above, and remove with the hair and skin the pus from under the nail which dries up the inflammation. And similarly, you follow that with the hair inside the anus of the patient.
And then you insert the remnants into the root of the eyelash with a thin spatula or small forceps, and cut the flesh of the eyelid to allow for insertion of that without causing continuous flow of tears from it.
And sometimes the nail with only one ounce of gold or bile, as we said before, is extracted with a lion-shaped spatula of this form.
And make sure with the spatula not to touch the corneal tissue and that it breaks, and that the pupil is pierced.
Then make an incision in the ear with a small amount of triple salt or crushed onion and leave it inside for another day, and then treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
And if the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert the needle, nor has it been inserted with an ounce of gold, then many times this type of nail is cured with medications, as mentioned before, in a similar way to how eyes are treated and recommended in that section.
And if you want to make an incision, then open the ear of the patient and take a thin lion-shaped spatula with sharpness according to this form: With subtlety (or finesse). And if sometimes the ear is rarefied and congested and filled in that area, then distill your medicine into the ear made of crushed onion or chopped turnip or triple salt, and fill the ear for another day.
Then repeat that operation until everything in it has been expelled, unless a counteracting abscess is formed in the ear, then you should leave it alone and treat the abscess first before it heals.
Then repeat your operation on that with reason until it is healed.
If the swelling of the eyelid causes great harm, then suspend it with an ounce; and make an incision in that one part, and do not complete the incision so that you do not pierce the tear duct.
Then distill turnip juice and chopped onions in the eyelid until it is healed.
Chapter 17.
On incision of abscesses and things born from congested flesh in the eyelid.
Sometimes in the eyelids of some patients, red flesh is born and it covers the pupil or approaches and presses on the eyelids, making them almost close completely, and looks like a ballista wound.
But the treatment for this is that the patient holds their head upwards; and then you open the eyelids of the patient and collect all the red flesh with suitable weights, and use forceps or a small container; and then make an incision in the flesh starting from the beginning until it is finished with your appropriate instruments, and be careful not to damage the eyelid while carrying out this operation.
And your incision should be the one with which you make an incision using a spatula that we recommended in the treatment of nails, or using small forceps according to the shape described later in this chapter.
Once your incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, then fill the eyelid with triple salt, or instill red powder similar to corrosive medicine, and place over it a bandage made of egg white outside until it is protected from an opposing abscess.
And if there remains any reason for abscesses and it is bleeding with pus, and you are worried about an opposing abscess, then leave the eyelid alone and treat the abscess first with what will cure that, and repeat your operation on it until it heals completely, and similarly do the same with congested flesh that can occur in this type of eyelid.
But however, you must keep all treatment of the eyelid free from any natural or accidental injury, caused by tools and not to touch it with your hands in any of these operations until you see that the member is ready for this operation.
Chapter 18.
On collecting pus in the eyelid.
Pus is red veins that appear on the eyelid and prevent urination by blocking its function, causing it to swell for several days.
Therefore, it is necessary at the beginning to first determine whether the eyelid where pus has formed is otherwise healthy and only affected by pus; then you can proceed to collect that pus.

Chapter 30.
On the Extraction of Teeth.
It is important to carefully cure the tooth of its pain before attempting to extract it, taking your time and using all necessary precautions during the extraction process, because there is no substitute for the missing part of the tooth once it has been removed. This is due to the fact that the remaining substance of the tooth is sublime and cannot be replaced through extraction alone.
However, when the patient is forced to undergo tooth extraction, it is essential that you are absolutely certain which tooth is causing the pain, as patients can often mistake the source of their discomfort and believe that a healthy tooth is causing the problem. It is important to extract the correct tooth in order to effectively address the pain, because we have seen through experience that the pain will not subside until the actual diseased and painful tooth has been removed, just as we have observed during barber surgery operations.
Therefore, when you are certain which tooth is causing the pain, and you know this well, then it is necessary to scarify the area around the tooth with a spatula containing some kind of healing agent or medicine, in order to dissolve the tooth from the gums all the way around. After that, use the tools that I have mentioned, such as small forceps, to carefully and gradually loosen the tooth until it is removed.
And then apply strong forceps or large tweezers to the tooth in order to have a good grip and maintain control over it. Hold the patient's head firmly between your hands, ensuring that they do not move or cause any harm. Then carefully extract the tooth, pulling it straight out in a smooth motion, being careful not to break it or cause further pain to the patient.
And so, if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments and gently insert it beneath the tooth from all sides with ease and force, in order to begin the process of removing it.
However, if the tooth is broken or corroded, then it is necessary to first wrap it with a piece of cloth and then use a thin wire to securely fasten the cloth around the tooth, in order to prevent it from breaking further during extraction.
It is important to carefully scarify the gums all around the tooth and use great care and precision in order to avoid breaking or damaging the tooth further during extraction. Be sure to maintain your strength and control throughout the procedure, as the patient may become more resistant to the pain after the initial stages of treatment.
And be sure not to make the same mistakes as some ignorant barbers do in their haste and recklessness during extractions, without administering the treatments that we have recommended. This can lead to serious complications for the patient, which may be difficult or impossible to correct. Additionally, be careful not to extract teeth along with bones from the jaw or other parts of the body, as we have seen in some cases.
And then clean and rinse the patient's mouth with vinegar or wine mixed with salt after extracting the tooth.
If excessive bleeding occurs after the extraction, as is often the case, then apply a small amount of crushed garlic to the wound and sprinkle it with powdered herbs. If this does not stop the bleeding, then use a hot iron to cauterize the area and seal the wound.
The shape of the forceps and thin tweezers used to grip the tooth at the beginning should have a long handle, a short grip, and a thick head, in order to prevent them from bending or breaking during use.
And similarly, the handles of these tools should be thick and sturdy, in order to prevent them from bending or breaking when applied with force. The heads of the tools, on the other hand, should be slender and agile, allowing for precise movements and manipulation during extraction procedures.
The forceps and tweezers used for tooth extraction should be made of high-quality iron, with straight handles that are evenly balanced and aligned. The heads of these tools should feature interlocking teeth that can grip the tooth securely and apply steady pressure during extraction. In some cases, the heads may also have a curved or hooked shape, similar to the beak of a stork (known as 'ciconia'), which can provide additional strength and precision during the procedure.

Chapter 35.
On the removal of a ranula beneath the tongue.
Sometimes, small abscesses can appear under the tongue that resemble a small nodule and prevent the tongue from performing its normal functions. The procedure for removing such an abscess involves opening the patient's mouth wide in front of a window or other source of natural light, and carefully examining the abscess to assess its size and location. (Note: it is important to ensure adequate lighting and visibility during the procedure to avoid causing unnecessary harm.)
And if you see that it is of a dark or black color and hard, without sensation in the patient, then do not touch it as it is a tumor. (Note: a hard, insensate mass beneath the tongue could be indicative of a malignant growth or other serious condition that requires further evaluation and treatment by a medical professional.)
If it has turned white and is moist, then you should place a probe into it and make an incision with a sharp lancet, cutting through all parts of the abscess. If bleeding occurs during the procedure, then apply a compress of vitriol to stop it. (Note: this procedure involves making an incision in a soft tissue abscess to drain it and promote healing. However, caution must be exercised to avoid causing unnecessary damage or bleeding.)
And then return to your work and complete the treatment until it is healed, washing it with vinegar and salt. Attend to it with the other treatments mentioned in this chapter until it is cured. (Note: this final sentence emphasizes the importance of following through with treatment and monitoring the patient's progress until healing is complete.)
Chapter 36.
Of the extraction of a abscess from both ears and of one that is located in the throat and of other abscesses.
When it happens in the throat, these are glands that are gathered and swollen, which come outwards and are called tonsils, which when you treat them with what we have said in the division and they do not heal, then you consider whether the abscess is hard, of dark color, with little sensation, then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and the tissue is large, then do not touch that with iron because of the flow of blood; first let it mature inside, and then either you will surgically remove it or it will break open by itself.
And if it is of white color, soft, and its tissue is fine, then that one needs to be incised.
And the procedure is that you consider before your operation whether the abscess has rested enough after caution or if it has decreased in size; and then make the patient face the sun, and their head should be by your side, and hold open their mouth, and the servant holding between their hands firmly presses down the patient's tongue with a noble instrument of which this is the form:
And it should be made of silver or iron, and be as thin as a knife.
And as you press with that instrument on the tongue and reveal the abscess, then place your finger over it and apply pressure; then take a probe and insert it into the opening, and pull it outwards as far as possible. Or if you extract some cause from the membranes (of the abscess), then appropriately make an incision with this instrument of which this is the form:
Or if you extract some cause from the membranes (of the abscess), then appropriately make an incision with this instrument of which this is the form: and it is shaped like forceps, but the ends of it are curved inward so that the opening of each side faces the other, making them very sharp, made of iron that has been heated.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then make an incision with a spatula of which this is the shape: It should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other.
And after you have made an incision on one side, make another incision on the other side using this same method of incision, and then dress the wound with warm water.
But if there is a flow of blood, dress the wound with an infusion of elderberry bark or myrtle leaves and similar astringent causes until the flow of blood has been restricted, and then treat it until it heals.
And sometimes other abscesses occur in the throat besides the tonsils, and you should incise those using the same method as for two abscesses.
And I once treated a woman with an abscess that had formed in her throat, which was dark in color and had little sensation, and she had already closed off her throat, and the woman was breathing with difficulty, and she had been prohibited from eating or drinking water for some time, and she was on the verge of death if she had gone without treatment for another day or two.
And the abscess had already grown so large that it took two months to drain through two openings.
And so I cautiously inserted one of my fingers into one of the openings and pulled out a large portion of it, and then I made an incision where I thought the other opening was, and then I opened her mouth wide, compressed her tongue, and inserted my finger into that abscess.
And then I cut away a large portion of it, and only a small amount of blood flowed out. And so the woman's throat was healed, and she immediately began to drink water and eat solid food again. But I continued to incise the abscess several times over a long period of time, and another abscess formed in place of the first one, which I kept incising until it had been completely drained.
And then I put a hot iron on her throat to cauterize it, and that was the end of it. But as for what God did with that abscess in relation to me, I do not know.
Chapter 37.
On incising a whirl (or swelling) when it is abscessed.
When there is a catarrh in the whirl, and it is abscessed and long, then it is called a "perpendicular" one; but if it is large and round in the lower part, then it is called a "bubble."
But when it is healed with what we have said in the division, and you do not find satisfaction in your treatment, sometimes an abscess that has been cauterized remains as a scar, which is thin; and if it is round and attached to the longitude, and is bloody, of dark color or black, and does not feel hot, then you must be careful when making an incision there, because in that case there is fear for the patient.
And when you see it according to the method I have described based on its whiteness and length, then you should make the patient lie down and press their tongue with an instrument that was mentioned earlier, and then insert a probe into the new opening and pull it downward, making an incision with one of two instruments that were previously mentioned.
And it is necessary that you do not make an incision there unless it is at the end of the natural term, without addition, because if you make an incision beyond that, you will damage their voice.
And during the incision, use what we recommended earlier in the section on two abscesses, and treat it until it is healed.
But if the patient is frightened by the incision, it is necessary to use caution in the cauterization process and avoid causing unnecessary fear. The method of cauterization involves using hot water, which you should apply as follows: have the patient's head on your side, press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier, then take the hot water that we discussed in the chapter on cauterization, and use it to moisten a piece of linen or wool. Place this inside the concavity of the cauterizing instrument, which is shaped like this:
Let the external part of the concavity where the medicine is placed be shaped like a round-bottomed flask, and place the instrument with the medicine on top of the abscess. Have the patient lie down on their side so that any saliva or mucus from their mouth does not flow over the incision site, which could cause further damage.
And place your hand with the medicine over the abscess, and press it gently for a quarter of an hour until you see that the area has turned black and become numb due to the action of the medicine.
If you wish, take some cotton and wrap it around the tip of the flask. Then submerge the cotton in the medicine and insert the flask with the cotton into a larger tube or cannula. Make sure that the cotton adheres to the inside of the cannula, then repeat this process several times until you have achieved the desired level of cauterization for the abscess. Then allow the area to dry and fall off on its own after three or four days.
If you find it necessary to reapply the medicine, do so. Then clean the area around the abscess with a piece of cloth soaked in vinegar and water, and remove any remaining medicine from the surface of the skin. Wash the area with warm water and soap, then apply an embrocation (a type of medicated ointment) to the outside. Inside, use dressing changes until the wound heals completely.
This type of cure is safer than incision and longer, but less risky.
Sometimes the uvula is cured with something more subtle than cauterization or incision, which is done through sublimation in this way: take calamint, hyssop, oregano, rue, Arabic zeds, chamomile, ground and similar herbs to those, and combine all of these causes or some of them in a bowl, and submerge them with sour wine and boil. The bowl should be well cleaned with clean water, and there should be a hole in the middle of the bowl, on which an instrument hollowed out of steel is placed like this: it should be made of silver or steel.
And the end of the instrument should be inserted into the patient's mouth until the steam reaches the abscess and causes it to become obscured or darkened. This suggests that the sublimation process can cause the tissue in the area to temporarily change color, indicating that the medicine has taken effect.
And repeat this treatment several times until the abscess dries up. However, do not use sublimation at the beginning of an abscess outbreak, as it may aggravate the condition and cause further swelling or infection. Instead, wait until the abscess has formed before attempting to treat it with sublimation.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then take a straw and make a hole in one end of it, so that the patient's mouth can be propped open. This prevents the steam from burning their mouth or throat during treatment.
And this cure is good for health. (or: And this treatment is beneficial for health)
Chapter 38.
On the extraction of splinters and things that stick in the throat, as well as other causes.
Often, lumps or swellings adhere in the throat, or a splinter of fish bone, or some other cause.
