And what is not visible and hidden in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before food is digested in the stomach, because often the adhered cause will easily come out through vomiting; or have the patient chew a piece of napkin or lettuce leaf or a piece of dry bread; or take a piece of dry sea sponge and soak it strongly with bile, then give it to the patient to swallow, for when it reaches the location where the splinters are, they will be expelled. Or take an eel and tie it up with bile, place it on a plate and then extract it after it has been swallowed; or take a piece of bread and insert it into the throat and pull it out again.
Or if they are not expelled by those methods mentioned earlier, then use an instrument made of lead in this way:
And it should be slightly thicker than a finger, and on its outer surface should be a concavity that you can insert with ease into the patient's throat.
And it should have its head raised upwards, and make sure that the contact with the patient's throat is not too hard, so that it touches only the skin and catches any growth or splinter, or guides it gently with its hand.
But it is better if the patient himself can insert it, using his knowledge of the location of the adhered cause and pushing it downwards, while pulling up on the instrument with his hand, all according to the size of the object that needs to be extracted.
Chapter 39. (Note: As mentioned earlier, chapters were often numbered using Roman numerals in medieval manuscripts)
On the removal of a bloodsucker attached to the throat. (Note: "Sangüisuga" is an old word for a leech or other type of parasite that feeds on blood, and "annexa" means "attached.")
When a bloodsucker is treated with what we have discussed in the section on medical treatment and not by means of cupping glasses, look carefully at the patient's throat and press the tongue forward with an instrument that I have recommended to you.
Therefore, if you see the bloodsucker, extract it gently with a pair of tweezers or some other delicate instrument.
And if you are unable to extract it with the tweezers, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's throat, place a heated iron in the concavity of the cannula, do this several times (until the bloodsucker is dead and detaches from the throat) and ensure that the patient abstains from water for the entire day.
And then take a horn full of water and rinse the mouth with it, and have the patient drink some of that water and keep it in their mouth for an hour or two without swallowing, because as soon as the bloodsucker feels the water it will come out on its own.
But if it is not expelled by the methods we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with cumin or asafoetida using the instrument that we have recommended in the section on fumigation of the uvula.
Do it in this way, four times. (Note: "Cayra" is an old word for "time.")
Here is another method of operation in fumigation of the bloodsucker: take a pot with burning coals inside and cover it with a cloth, and place a hole in the middle of the cloth where the end of the instrument can be inserted; then perform the fumigation from above; and place the patient's mouth over the end of the cannula and close their lips so that the fumigation is not lost before you are sure that it has reached the bloodsucker, because as soon as the bloodsucker feels the fumigation it will come out.
And if it does not come out, then you should repeat the fumigation many times and ensure that the patient abstains from drinking water, eats salty foods and garlic, and avoids water completely. This is necessary to ensure that the bloodsucker is expelled.
And this is the shape of the instrument used to treat bloodsuckers in the throat when they are visible; it resembles tweezers but has a slight curve. (Note: The sentence describes the shape of an instrument used for removing bloodsuckers from the throat, which should have a slight curve.) and place it in the throat, with its tip resembling the beak of a stork, which is curved and sharpened with a file, so that when compressing any object, it does not slip away.
Chapter 40. (Note: As mentioned earlier, chapters were often numbered using Roman numerals in medieval manuscripts)
In which is the summary of the discourse on abscesses and their classification. (Note: "Apercio" means overview or summary, and "apostemas" refers to abscesses)
Abscesses are of many types and kinds, as will be remembered from the descriptions in this book. (Note: The sentence acknowledges that there are many different types of abscesses, each with its own characteristics.)
And they are differentiated by penetration and section in two ways: one is according to the type of abscess, and the other is due to their moisture content. (Note: The sentence suggests that abscesses can be classified based on their type and moisture content.)
And the second way is based on the location in which they occur, as an abscess that occurs in the head is different from one that occurs in the buttocks, and an abscess that occurs in a fleshy area is different from one that occurs at a joint; each requires its own treatment.
And some abscesses must not be pierced until the pus in them has matured or their development is complete.
Some abscesses need to be pierced when they are still fresh and not yet mature, such as those that occur near joints or the groin area. When an abscess is located near a joint, its development takes longer because it spreads in the surrounding tissue, which can cause damage to the ligaments or nerves of that joint, leading to contraction of the limb. If the abscess is near the main part of the body, it is essential not to delay piercing it until it matures, as this may lead to injury to the main organ. Similarly, an abscess located in the buttocks should be pierced before it matures to avoid damage to the surrounding tissue and prevent the formation of a fistula or an unhealed wound. However, it is not necessary to make a large incision; instead, a small opening can be made to allow the pus to drain out. However, it is important to know the right time for piercing an abscess, and that is when it has matured.
And know that an abscess is mature when the pain and fever have subsided, as well as the inflammation and pulse rate, and the swelling at the tip of the abscess has become soft and there are signs of pus formation. (Note: The sentence lists some of the indications that an abscess has matured and is ready to be pierced.)
It is important to know that the incision should be made in a location below the abscess, where the pus will flow from the cure of the elevation. (Note: The sentence advises that the incision for piercing an abscess should be made in a location below it, allowing the pus to flow out freely and prevent further spread of infection.)
And the incision should always be made in the direction of the flesh or body, even if the abscesses are on the sides of the hands or feet, and on the ligaments, nerves, and arteries; and finally, in all places where there is no danger of reflection. For in those that reflect, use incision according to the member.
However, when the abscess is located in a fleshy area, it is better to wait until the digestion of the abscess has been confirmed before making an incision, as I have said. This is because if you pierce it before then, the contents will spill out and mix with the surrounding tissue, causing further inflammation and making the wound more difficult to heal. By waiting until the abscess has fully matured, the risk of complications is reduced and healing is facilitated.
However, some abscesses must be pierced according to the width of the flesh or body depending on necessity, or according to what the member requires.
It is important to make a small incision in small abscesses and a larger one in large abscesses, with multiple sections if necessary according to the diversity of their size. (Note: The sentence emphasizes that the size of the incision should be proportional to the size of the abscess.)
And other abscesses require that the skin be excised and turned inside out, when it is necessary to make a cavity as in cases of tuberculosis and scrofula. (Note: The sentence refers to certain types of abscesses that require more extensive surgical intervention, such as excision of the affected area and creation of a cavity or wound.)
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles, there is one in which it is incised as the shape of a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses of hernias. (Note: The sentence describes two different types of incisions used to treat abscesses, depending on their size and location. In some cases, a triangular incision may be made, while in others a curved or myrtle-leaf shaped incision may be more appropriate.)
And of them are those in which a round section or crescent-shaped incision is made, similar to these. (Note: The sentence describes two more types of incisions used to treat abscesses, depending on their shape and location. A round incision may be appropriate for small, shallow abscesses, while a crescent-shaped incision may be used for larger or deeper ones.)
But if it is not like those deep-seated abscesses that require a more extensive incision, then a superficial or shallow puncture may be sufficient. (Note: The sentence suggests that in some cases, a simple incision or puncture may be all that is needed to treat an abscess.)
And it is important to note that when the abscess is large and has accumulated a lot of pus, you should make an incision in it but do not be hasty to drain all of the pus at once; instead, remove only a portion of it and then pack the wound with sterile gauze or bandages. Repeat this process daily until the entire abscess has been drained. (Note: This approach allows for controlled drainage of the abscess over several days, reducing the risk of infection and promoting optimal healing.)
And especially if the patient is of frail constitution, or a woman in labor, or a small child, or an elderly person in decrepitude, since the animal spirit often becomes weakened with the expulsion of blood, and the patient can quickly die, and you should open the veins.
Observe this chapter with great caution, and direct your incision in the place where you lance these abscesses; it is necessary that you clean the wounds and consider whether the abscess has a small opening or is a wide incision; therefore, you should apply some of the medicines of honey or vinegar; and if the abscess is large, and the slits of the incision are many, then it is necessary for you to place a wick in each hole so that they can drain together.
And if part of the colon is cut off in the abscess or has become concave in its circumference, then it is necessary for you to compress it with old linen or a thread made of wool cloth, just as when you bandage wounds or cuts, without moisture; and strengthen that within the third day; and then treat and care for it with appropriate ointments until it heals.
But if you encounter bleeding during your operation, then apply a cloth soaked in wine and water, which should be wrung out, over the site of the blood flow, as many times as necessary.
But if the bleeding persists, then it is necessary for you to provide treatment and care and use powders that I have recommended in many places of this our book and division.
But if it is winter and the location of the abscess is a place with many nerves, then it is necessary for you to apply poultices made of wine and warm oil over those areas.
And if it is summer and the location is fleshy, then it is necessary for you to apply poultices made of water and oil or wine and oil, and everything should be applied until the third day, as we have said; and then it is necessary for you to open the abscess, clean it, and provide treatment for healing until it heals.
And this is what is necessary for the understanding of the treatment of abscesses in general; but according to the method of distinction, I have already discussed each type of abscess and its specific method of healing in separate chapters.
Chapter 41.
Chapter 41: On Incisions for Abscesses that Occur in the Scalp.
In the scalp, small abscesses occur that are of the nature of nodes and contain tunics in their formation; and there are many types of these.
And from them come pustules, and some contain moisture similar to lime. And there are those that contain moisture similar to sand and resemble it; and there are those that are stony, hard.
And in the incision and removal of all of these, there is no fear, as long as you avoid doing it too forcefully.
And the operation in incising these is that you probe them with an instrument called a trocar, which has a shape appropriate for this, until you are certain of what they contain.
Because if it contains moisture, then you should cut it open with an incision in the shape of a surface slit, according to this form.
Begin the incision on the line of B going toward the line of G. Once the moisture has been evacuated, then you should excise the area that contained it, leaving no residue at all; for if any residue remains, it may cause further abscesses to form.
Then submerge the area in Egyptian ointment if it is available, and if not, in water and salt; and fill the wound with this substance, leaving it for another day, as it will dissolve all that remains of the membrane.
Then apply a second and third layer of Egyptian ointment to the area as needed, until you are confident that there is no residue left from the membrane; after this, care for the wound with an ointment until it heals.
And if the abscess contains fatty nodes, then you should make an incision according to this form: Having made an incision in the shape of a cross, you should then cut between the two lips of the incision and remove all parts of it; and exert your strength in extracting the membrane that contains it.
But if you encounter resistance, then do what I have told you to do first (i.e., make an incision along the length of the abscess and excise the area that contained it).
And similarly, proceed with the incision and treatment of the stony abscess as I have told you; and incising over a stony abscess is easier because it contains little blood and moisture.
Sometimes the abscesses in the scalp of some men contain no moisture at all; this is due to the fact that it cannot be incised on because there is no humidity present. This is similar to what happened when I attempted to make an incision on the abscess of an old woman's head, and found it to be as hard as a stone, rough, white, and unyielding; if anyone were to strike against such a growth, they would cause harm to themselves.
But in the other types of abscesses that occur on the head, such as those that appear on children's heads and must be cut along their ear rims, the incision for these should be made using surface cuts.
And position the puncture holes of these in the lower area, to help relieve the body of blood and moisture in the lower areas.
And then care for these wounds with what is appropriate for their healing.
Chapter 42.
Chapter 42: On Incisions for Scrofula That Occur on the Neck.
These abscesses often occur in the neck, armpits, and groins, but they can also appear in other areas of the body.
And those that occur in the neck are often generated between them, and all scrofulous growths of this type are within their own membrane, just as with nodes and abscesses on the head, as we have previously discussed.
And the types of scrofula are numerous, as some are stony and hard, others contain moisture, and still others are malignant and do not respond to treatment.
Therefore, for the type of scrofula that you judge to be in good condition and whose visible color is similar to the color of the scalp, and it is soft everywhere, and not attached to the neck nerves, veins, or arteries, and is not bulging, then you should make a dry surface incision from the upper part of the body to the lower part along the line between G and B, as we have discussed for abscesses on the head. Then excise all parts of it, and separate the skin of the neck with an ounce or more if necessary, as we have described before. And then extract it bit by bit.
It is important to be careful not to cut the vein or nerves. (Note: This sentence appears to summarize and reinforce the previous passage's caution against cutting into the neck's nerves, veins, or arteries.)
It is necessary that the scalpel not be too sharp or unsettling to the patient, and that it only cuts what needs to be cut; for if you were to cut a vein or artery, this would prevent you from continuing your operation. In such cases, apply vinegar or other powders that can stop the bleeding and strengthen the wound, allowing the swelling of the abscess to subside and the wound to become softer and begin to turn black. When blood has been cut (or "when the cutting of blood occurs") or when bleeding starts during surgery, it is important to apply pressure or a styptic agent to stop the bleeding and prevent further damage. This can be done using a variety of methods, such as cauterization, ligation, or the application of hemostatic agents. In this context, vinegar or other powdered substances may have been used for their styptic properties, which help to contract blood vessels and promote clotting.
Therefore, return to your operation until you have completed it. (Note: This sentence summarizes the previous discussion and emphasizes the importance of continuing with the medical procedure.)
And then inquire with your skilled touch if there is any residue from other small scrofula growths, and if so, cut into those and clean them out. (Note: The word "teiu" means "skilled" or "expert". Here it refers to the sense of touch used in medical examination.)
And if it is on the edge of a large vein, then it is necessary not to cut into that scrofula at its edges. Before, take a piece of folded cloth soaked in strong bile and leave it inside so that it can fall out by itself and cause no harm.
Then fill the wound with old goat's dung, which you have previously soaked in Egyptian ointment, and heal it.
And if you find that the entire scrofulous sore is infiltrated, then it is necessary to bring together the two sides of the wound and quickly sew it up so that no excess fluid remains.
But if you see that there is excess fluid due to the size of the scrofulous sore, then it is necessary to consider incising the edge of it and draining that fluid away before administering stitches as previously described.
And for scrofulous sores containing moisture, make a superficial incision at the place where you see signs of maturation, and then place the incision at the lowest point of the body as we have said before.
Then administer incisions, using cauterization and similar substances to eat away at what has been opened due to corruption. Then when you see the wound is already cleaned out, heal it with flesh-generating ointment until it heals completely.
Chapter XLIII.
Of the sectioning of the head of the abscess located within the groin area.
The ancients recommended this sectioning in the head of an abscess, but I have not seen any person in our land who has done it.
And this is the inscription of the saying of those [ancients].
But in men with hip pain, it is necessary to avoid extracting the head of an abscess because this could bring no benefit since all major veins and arteries of the patient are located here.
But for those who have abscesses in the mouth or groin or both ears, when the illness is not located in the spine, it is necessary to make an incision on the head of an abscess to prevent the danger brought about by pus formation.
Therefore, it is advisable to make an incision on the head of an abscess below three circles or four within the circumference of the abscess head, with a small section along its length at the point where two circles meet, ensuring that the incision is made in skin and not cartilage. This location is suitable for incision since it lacks flesh and has blood vessels running through it.
And if the physician is inexperienced, then it is recommended that they extend the groin strap with an ounce and make a slit on the strap until it reaches the canal, while avoiding blood vessels for any reason.
Then make an incision on the lips as we have recommended, and mark the section of the canal with a flame, which will emerge from it due to the rupture and abscess formation in the vocal cords.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, when the time comes to close the wound and avoid incision, attach two sides of the groin strap to the wound, making sure not to include any cartilage in the stitches.
Then administer medications that promote tissue growth until the wound heals completely.
And Albucasis says that the essence of this teaching we have recommended is simply to show that some cases of abscesses have already filled the patient's groin area, leading them to death and suffocation, with their breath trapped inside. Therefore, surgeons must incise the epiglottis to allow the patient to breathe through the wound, thereby saving them from certain demise.
And so I command that the wound be left open until the harmful effects of the disease have been eliminated, which usually takes three days. Afterward, I recommend stitching up the wound and treating it until it heals completely.
And what I have personally witnessed is that a maidservant took a knife and inserted it into her own groin, cutting through one part of the lung's ribcage. I was called to treat her injury, and upon examination, I found her in a state similar to that of a dying person's moan, with an open wound gushing out small amounts of blood from within.
Therefore, I confessed that she had not cut any vein or artery, but rather the blood was flowing out of the wound itself. I treated her injury until it healed completely.
And the maidservant did not suffer any significant harm besides losing her voice, and after several days, she regained her strength and normal functions.
And now I say that there is no fear in making an incision on the head of an abscess.
Chapter XLIV.
Of the incision on an abscess that occurs in the outer groin area, and is called a hernia of the groin.
This unnamed abscess, commonly referred to as a hernia of the groin, is a large swelling depending on the complexion of the body and is common in women.
This condition can occur in two ways: either naturally or accidentally.
And for those that occur naturally, there is no cure.
An accidental hernia can occur in two ways, one of which resembles fatty nodes, and the other is similar to an abscess caused by a knot in an artery. In this latter case, there is cause for concern. And one should not be overly presumptuous when using surgical tools, except in cases of small hernias. You should examine such hernias carefully and investigate them with the aid of the aforementioned tools. If you find it resembles fatty nodes and is not suspended by any veins, then proceed to incise it in the same manner as you would for nodes, extracting the contents along with the surrounding tissue and membrane. However, if this is not the case, then thoroughly scrutinize its entire structure, and treat the area with appropriate remedies until it heals completely.
Chapter 45
Of the section on types of knots (or swellings).
There are many types of knots, and I have already mentioned all the types in the previous section.
And it is necessary for me to explain further the difference between a knot (or swelling) and an abscess, as there may be some confusion.
Therefore, I say that an abscess is characterized by heat, fever, and intense pain, as long as the boiling of the excess fluid has not yet been alleviated. Once the abscess reaches its full stage of putrefaction, it stops causing fever, pain, and heat.
But a knot (or swelling) is not characterized by heat, fever, or pain, and it includes a hard lump like a "ciphac leon" that forms in its own sack.
And it is also according to the color of the body that we can determine its type, and at first it resembles a goiter and develops in a similar way as a bladder, whether large or small. It is divided into two types: one is fatty and contains moisture, and the moisture has many colors, as I have said in the previous section.
Therefore, when you come to the treatment of the knot, it is necessary to remove it and inquire about its beginning with an instrument called "intromes," according to its shape, as described in the following chapter.
And this is the method of inquiry for abscesses and all types of knots: that you take this instrument (intromes) and insert it into the most humid part of the abscess that you find, and then you rotate it gently, little by little, until you are certain that the instrument has penetrated the core.
Then place your hand according to the size of the abscess and remove the intromes (medical probe) and observe what comes out in its trace.
And if the running moisture of any color has been released, then you should cut it with a superficial incision, as I have said for other abscesses.
And if there is no moisture coming from the trace of the probe, then you know that it is fat (or a fatty abscess).
And make an incision over it in the shape of a cross, like this: and cut it open in the shape of a cross as I have taught you, and suspend it with a ligature, and carefully remove the core from all sides, and preserve the skin or sac if possible over it, and extract the pus with the abscess.
But if it bursts during the operation, it is not possible to extract healthy tissue, and many times this results in the opposite outcome. Therefore, you should extract (the abscess) with pressure until none of it remains.
Because if any cause remains, whether little or too much, the abscess will return according to its severity.
And if you see that some small part remains, then fill the wound with some sharp and corrosive powders and strengthen the area, and place a cauterizing agent on the abscess, and cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
And if it is a large abscess, then you should suture the two lips of it and cure it with what fleshes (or matures).
But if the pulse is moving towards it (the abscess) or not pulsating, then you should place and fill the area with three times sixty of quicksilver (mercury), which is called "vetriol," and leave it straight for two days or three until the wound can be opened again and the boiling of the blood has subsided; and then return to cutting what remains of the abscess.

Chapter 47.
On the treatment of male breasts, which resemble those of women.
Sometimes, the breasts of some men become inflamed due to excessive sleep and begin to resemble those of women, and they also develop abscesses that are far from the nipples.
And for those who have this condition, it is necessary to make an incision with a crescent shape along the line from B to G, and then remove all of the thickened tissue, fill the wound with a carmine-colored medicine, suture the two sides of the wound together, and treat the inside so that it heals.
But if the breast sags towards the lower parts and becomes soft like those of women, then it should be cut in two along its upper part with two incisions that are similar to a crescent shape, and each one should fit inside the other until the larger one contains the smaller one, according to this form of the line B and the line G. Then remove the fatty tissue between the two sides of the wound, administer what we have said about suturing and powders, and continue treatment until it heals.
And if you do not complete the incision as necessary due to the patient's discomfort or excessive bleeding, then it is necessary to apply a compress soaked in corrosive ointment to the wound and let the corrosive substance break down the thickened tissue until it becomes soft. Then treat the inside of the wound until it heals.
Chapter 48.
On the incision of abscesses that form in the lower parts due to itching.
These abscesses that form in the lower parts due to itching are of the type called scrofula, which contain a pus-like substance.
And some of these abscesses contain moisture, and those that do should be incised with a crescent-shaped incision along the line from G to B, as shown in this figure. Once all of the pus has been evacuated from the abscess and it is clean, then apply a dry compress and leave it on for another day.
And then apply a dry compress and treat it with appropriate ointment until it heals.
And if the abscess is of the type with nodes or is a scrofula, then incise it as we have said in the section on scrofulas.
But if the wound extends to an area where it can be cauterized, then apply cautery as we have said before.
Chapter 49.
On the incision of abscesses caused by an artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured and the tissue around it has hardened, often an abscess forms. The signs that indicate an inflammation or abscess caused by an artery or vein are: when an abscess is due to an artery, it will be long and located in a prominent part of the body; and when you press on the abscess with your fingers, you can hear a stridor sound.
And an abscess caused by a vein will be round and visible on the surface of the body.
And sectioning above this abscess is a mistake, especially in one that is below the armpits, and in the groin, and in the neck, and in many other parts of the body; and it is very large, so its surgical treatment should be avoided, and one that is on the limbs or the head should be prevented.
But as for one that is located due to inflammation of the orifice of the artery, make an incision in the longitudinal section in the groin; and then separate the incision with forceps and expose the artery, and free it from the tunics that cover it.
And then place a needle over it and make it penetrate into the other side, and strengthen the artery with double tanned leather in two places - which causes a tightening in the extraction of two arteries that are in the temples.
And then place your finger on the location that is between two ligaments with a spatula until all of the blood is drained from it, and let the abscess be resolved.
And then administer treatment that generates pus inside until the ligaments give way; and then cure it with appropriate ointments until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess due to incision of a vein, then you should hold with your hand as much as possible of the abscess towards the groin, and then insert the needle below the location that you have held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and let there be double thread in it as you extract it from the other side, and then tie off the abscess with a good ligament as I have told you in the grape-like ligament of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you are afraid of extracting the thread, then insert tanned leather with that needle below the entire abscess and strengthen the incision with the thread in four places.
And then dry out the abscess in the middle of it until what is inside it comes out, and then incise the excess skin of the groin, and let what adheres to it remain.
And then place over it the poultice that you have soaked in wine and oil, and then administer the treatment that is made with warm compresses and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 1: The abscess that occurs due to nerve twisting.
Just as an abscess occurs in the artery and vein, so too does an abscess occur in the nerves when it occurs due to nerve compression or excessive work, among other things.
And it is most often found in the areas of the adductors or ankle, or in any location where the joints are strained.
And it is a severe abscess, and it resembles the color of other flesh, and it is located in the largest part of the limb, and when it becomes tight with intensity, the patient appears to be in a state of stupor.
And it is not an abscess that has spread in the belly of the body, and so it does not involve the groin, and it affects all parts equally and does not extend to the front or back.
Therefore, in the case of those that are located in the joints, it is not advisable to encase them with iron, as this can easily lead to contraction.
But one that is in the head or forehead should be opened with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then extract it with forceps and cut it out at its roots.
And if it is large, then suspend it with forceps, and scrape it, and remove it; and close the wound with stitches, and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter 2.
Of incision of an abscess that occurs due to disease in the belly.
Often in the bellies of some people and in other parts of their bodies, there are swellings that are called fungal due to their similarity to mushrooms, the roots of which are subtle while the head is large; and the lips of these have turned inward, and they can be small or greatly enlarged.
And I have seen one that had two parts in his belly that resembled mushrooms more closely, and there was no difference between their white colors, as they had fine roots.
And the lips of these were turned inward and split open, and fluid flowed from it at all times.
Therefore I incised these and found in one of them a mass that weighed eighteen ounces. And the other weighed five ounces.
And the procedure in incising them is that you should consider whether the patient is moist, and if the color of the abscess is white, moist, with fine roots; then you should incise it with a broad spatula, and have cauteries present in the fire, because much fluid will be expelled from the incision, so if blood comes out, cauterize it.
And if you see that the patient is weak and fearful, be careful not to incise with iron; but rather take fresh lead filings, and strengthen the abscess with it in the manner that we have mentioned, and leave it for two days.
And then tighten the string of lead as it dissolves; therefore, do not stop strengthening the large piece of lead in the abscess, until it is cut and falls out by itself without any effort.
But if the abscess is of large roots, then there is reason to fear and be cautious in incising it, especially in one that is located in the belly.
But it is possible that you incise the entire abscess and then cauterize it to prevent its recurrence.
And then cure it until the wound heals.
And be careful not to assume that you can incise a tumor that is of dark color, with little sensation, and with irregular appearance, as this is likely cancerous.
And I will come back to remind you about cancer later.
Chapter II
Of the treatment of umbilical hernia.
The umbilical hernia is caused by many factors: either due to fissures of the ciphac which is above the belly and has its membrane or intestine protruding as in other ruptures, or due to blood that flows from a vein or artery as mentioned earlier, or due to constipation in it.
But if it is due to fissures of the ciphac and protrusion of the membrane, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is painless, and often appears in various forms. And if it is due to protrusion of the intestine, then its shape is similar to what we have mentioned, but with greater diversity, and as you press on it with your fingers, it disappears and then returns; and it can be easily pushed in, and becomes greatly enlarged when bathing and exertion.
But if it is due to moisture, then it is painless and does not disappear when pressed with the hand, nor is it constricted or swollen.
And if it is purulent, then use these signs to prepare for the abscess to ripen to a dark color.
But if it is caused by an accumulation of flesh, then the abscess is severe, large and hard, and swollen to a certain extent.
But if it is caused by gas, then touch it like a lion. (Note: I'm not sure about this translation as "leon" in old languages could also mean "boldly".)
And the procedure for this is to consider whether the prominence of the navel is due to an arterial or venous abscess, or to gas. If so, you must refrain from treating it, because, as taught in the chapter where I discussed abscesses of arteries and veins, there is danger and fear in such cases.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to an intestinal or tissue disorder, then you should instruct the patient to hold their own belly and stand upright. Then, using your finger, mark a circle around the entire navel, and place the patient lying down between your hands. Next, use a broad-bladed spatula to draw a line around the marked circle on the surface of the navel. Then, extend the base of the abscess upwards with a large incision; and finally, bind it in a circle with strong vinegar or cedar, using an appropriate binding method.
And then, insert your finger into the middle of the opened abscess and explore the tissue until you find the intestine; if you find it or feel it through the tissue, then gently pull it out and guide it back inside the abdomen.
And if you find tissue instead, then tie it with a ligature and cut away any excess.
But if it is contrary to your artery or vein, then tie it off and return to your operation. Take two needles and put strong threads on them, then insert the needles into the circle you made around the abscess like a cross, and pull the abscess in four parts onto the needles.
And if you wish, remove the needles and leave it alone until the flesh retracts and falls in by itself; or cut the thinned tissue carefully and suture the wound with appropriate sutures until it heals.
And if the prominence of the navel is due to flesh or moisture in it, then you should lance the abscess as we have said, and remove the pus or moisture that you find in it. Then treat it appropriately and solidify the area.
Chapter 53. (It seems like the text is starting a new chapter)
On the treatment of cancer.
We have already said in the division of types of cancer and how it can be cured with medicines, that treatment by surgery is not advisable because it causes ulcers. And we have also discussed the importance of caution and care in the treatment of cancer.
And the ancients said that some cancers are in places where it is possible to eradicate them entirely, such as cancer of the breast or groin and similar types located on limbs which allow for removal of all affected tissue, especially when they are starting out small.
But when it is old and large, you should not attempt to treat it, because I have never seen or heard of anyone being cured of such a severe cancer.
And the procedure for this is, when it is located as we have said, to proceed with caution and let the patient take some purgative medicine to cleanse the black bile from their system. Also, if there is obvious congestion, then bleed the patient.
And then, prepare the patient for surgery with a preparation that allows for the operation. Also, prohibit sharp objects near the incision, which is necessary. Additionally, make sure the area is thoroughly cleaned and free of any possible cause of infection. And let the blood flow freely and do not close it lightly. Express the wounds and wipe away the thick clots of blood with your hand or an appropriate instrument that is available to you.
But if the heavy bleeding is due to a cut vein or artery, then use a hot iron to cauterize it and stop the flow of blood, and treat the wound with other appropriate treatments until it heals.
Chapter 54. (It seems like the text is starting a new chapter)
On the treatment of dropsy.
We have already recommended in the division of types of dropsy and their symptoms, how to cure them with medicines.
And the type of dropsy that can be cured with surgery is only the type of ascites, and it should not be approached with a knife in cases of tympanites or hydrothorax, because that would be fatal.
And when you have treated this type of dropsy with tympanites using medicines and they do not respond to treatment, then consider whether the patient is already weakened or has another illness in addition to dropsy, such as cough or stomach pain, etc. If so, then refrain from treating them with surgery, because it is dangerous.
But if you see that the patient is strong and healthy, and their only illness is dropsy, and they are neither too young nor too old, then the method of operation for them is to lift the patient between your hands, place a bucket under their belly, have them press on their stomach with their own hand, push the water towards the lower part of the abdomen, and then take a pointed spatula in this way:
should be two-sided with sharp points like a spatula, but it should be short and gradually increase in length so that during the operation you do not penetrate the intestines, but only touch them.
And then consider whether the cause of dropsy is in some part of the intestines, because in that case, you should make your incision at a distance of three fingers below the navel on the right side towards the bladder.
But if the cause of dropsy is some illness of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the navel at a distance of three fingers.
And if the cause of dropsy is the spleen, then your incision should be on the right side.
And it is not advisable for your incision to be on the side where the patient wants to lie down, because then the excess fluids will accumulate in that place and cause harm.
And then use your instrument to make a hole in the abdominal wall and insert it into that incision, and lift your hand with the spatula between the abdominal wall and the intestines, and then you can clean out any excess fluid. The amount removed should be about the size of a fingernail or thereabouts.
And then pierce the intestines until the spatula reaches the empty space where the fluid is located. And then remove it and insert an instrument of this shape: (Note: The text does not provide a description of the shape, only says "of this shape" but there is no further explanation). and it resembles a slender silver cannula, made of silver or brass or lead, with a small hole at the lower end, and three holes on its sides: two on one side and one on the other side. The tip of this instrument is sharpened like a feather quill. (Note: I am providing a description based on the text).
And on the upper end of it is an armillary ring, so that when the instrument reaches the water, the ring can be placed on top of it, and this allows for drainage of the fluid in small quantities, because if too much fluid is drained at once, the patient may die from loss of vital spirits or suffer a stroke which could lead to death. (Note: I am providing a translation based on the text).
But drain it according to the strength of the patient and as indicated by their physical condition, the strength of their pulse, and overall health.
And then remove the instrument and keep the water that has accumulated due to the abdominal wall closing up the hole you made in it, which is why I instructed you to make an incision in that manner.
And then repeat the procedure the next day if you see that the patient tolerates it well, and drain a small amount of fluid each time for several days, but be careful not to leave too much fluid behind.
But if you are concerned about the patient, and leave too much fluid inside, then treat it with burial in warm sand, and apply heat to the area with a dry compress, and expose the affected area to the sun for a long time. Also, use drying medicines until the patient is healed.

But if you have an abscess or inflammation at the time of incision or at the time of cautery, or bleeding, then you must treat whatever problem you have with the appropriate treatment according to what is said.
But if the patient is weak and does not tolerate a second operation due to its horror, then perform puncture as we have recommended; and this is when you are certain, based on what has been said about the signs, that the hernia contains fluid.
Then it is necessary that you place the patient on an elevated cushion, and then puncture the abscess in the lowest part of it with a wide-bladed spatula, and place the puncture according to the length of the body.
And make the opening wide enough to drain all the water.
And then place a tight bandage over the area and leave it there, so that all remaining water is drained. And then care for it until the wound is healed.
But if there is resistance to the expulsion of water in that moment, then you should puncture it: and this is not done unless the white fatty tissue in the opening of the wound creates resistance and prevents the expulsion of water. In that case, it is necessary to insert a probe or instrument used to extract water from hydrops into the wound, with the same shape as before; or apply pressure to the area around the wound with a small piece of cloth.
And know that the water returns and accumulates again after about two or three months; and when it has accumulated, then it should be punctured in the same manner, because the patient will otherwise suffer through this.

Chapter 67.
On the dislocation that occurs in the ankles.

Chapter 68.

Chapter 69.
On Castration.
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, but it is necessary for me to mention it in this book; and its remembrance is required only for two reasons. The first reason is so that the physician knows how to treat it when questioned about it, as it may occur accidentally. The second reason is that we often have a need for castration of other animals for our livestock, such as horses, cattle, pigs, and similar beasts.
And so I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by constriction or through an incision.
But when it is performed by constriction, the method of operation is to place the animal in warm water until its genitals become soft and flaccid and hang down. Then take hold of them with your hand until they are relaxed and not visible underneath the skin.
But when castration is performed through an incision and sectioning, it is necessary to restrain the animal and press down on its lower back with your left hand.
Then tie off the spermatic cord and make an incision in each testicle along its length until two distinct sections are formed.
Then remove any excess tissue from the incisions made earlier. And make sure not to leave any tissue on the lower abdomen, but rather ensure that it is smooth and flat above the blood vessels.
And the method of castration through constriction is better because it leaves minimal tissue from the testicles, which reduces the desire for coitus in the animal.
Then care for the wound until it has healed completely.
Chapter 70.
On the Treatment of Hermaphrodites.
Hermaphrodites in men can be of two types: the first is when there is an extra space between the testicles, where a woman's labia would normally be located.
And sometimes this condition may cause the urine to flow from the scrotum instead of the urethra.
But in women, this condition is different: the labia of the female genitalia resembles two testicles in males, with one being slightly larger and protruding like the scrotum and the other being smaller and positioned further back.
And the treatment is of three kinds: two for men and one for women. It is necessary that you cut into the tight skin so as to release the pressure of it and then proceed to cure the other wounds/sores.
And in the second kind of men's ailment, where there is swelling in the codea (possibly meaning scrotum) of the testicles, there is neither cure nor operation for it.[Note: The word 'codea' is not anatomically correct but since medieval medical language isn't standardized, I assume this to be a variant or misnomer used during that time.]
Chapter 21.
On leanness and prominent flesh caused by women.
Leanness is easily noticeable in women, caused naturally when they are thin and in good health; but sometimes it becomes exaggerated in some women to such an extent that their bodies become as wide as men's, even affecting their ability to have intercourse.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to gather the excess leanness with your hand or tweezers and cut into it.
And do not cut too deeply, especially near the navel area, to avoid causing bleeding.
Then proceed to cure any wounds in the area until it heals completely.
Excessive flesh (carn nascuda) is the flesh that forms during pregnancy and fills up the mother's womb; it is easily noticeable when it bulges out of the body in a similar shape to a tail, which is why some call this condition "caudal disease". In such cases, it is necessary for us to cut into it just as we would with leanness and cure it until it heals completely.
Chapter 72.
On the treatment of hernia (alratica).
Hernia (alratica) refers to a condition where the woman's vagina is not properly perforated or has a small opening. And it can be either natural or accidental.
An accidental hernia is caused by a disease that has previously occurred, and it can be formed either due to loose skin or thin and subtle flesh. [Note: The text suggests that an accidental hernia can develop as a result of underlying medical conditions, weakened skin, or thin tissue.]
An accidental hernia can form in the navel of the mother, on her sides, at the upper part of her body, or lower down; it also restricts movement and physical activity such as lying down, lifting objects, and having intercourse, and often prevents menstruation from occurring. [Note: The text notes that an accidental hernia can limit a woman's ability to perform daily activities and impact her reproductive health.]
The diagnosis of this condition is made through observation by a midwife. If the opening is visible, then it can be easily diagnosed. However, if it's not apparent, then the physician or midwife should carefully examine the area using their fingers or a probe to detect any abnormalities. [Note: The text advises medical practitioners to use careful examination and observation in diagnosing hernias.]
But if the opening is due to thin flesh and located near the two labia, then you should sew it up and break open the thin flesh.
Then place your fingers on both labia majora, and carefully insert your thumbs between the labia minora, applying gentle pressure. [Note: The text advises medical practitioners to locate and press on the hernia with their thumbs while supporting the surrounding tissue with their fingers.]
And have the woman lie on her back with her buttocks raised and legs spread apart, then use force to pull open the two labia until the thin flesh is broken and the opening is revealed.
Then take some wool, soak it in oil and place it over the incision to prevent it from healing shut. Have someone check on the patient regularly to ensure that the incision does not become infected or closed before it is fully healed.
But if the tissue is thick and dense, then it is necessary to cut into it with a broad-bladed spatula or a myrtle leaf.
But if the opening is due to fatty tissue, then suspend it with forceps and cut into it.
And use the following medications that stop bleeding without causing pain, such as henbane, dragon's blood, spurge, and prepared with egg white.
Then administer a wide lead cannula to prevent the wound from healing too quickly.
And keep that in place for several days, and apply a poultice of dried figs to it.
Then cure it with the other method of healing by consolidation until it is healed completely.
And sometimes during childbirth, extra fleshy tissue forms, and it is necessary to cut into it using this method. Chapter 75
To teach midwives how to treat unborn children when there is a problem, according to the humoral theory.
It is necessary for the midwife to recognize at the beginning of childbirth by its signs whether it will be a natural birth or not. And so, when you see the woman pushing during labor and desiring to breathe in air, and becoming exhilarated because she feels relief from the weight of the baby on top of her, and she is hurrying to expel the fetus, then know that this delivery is according to a natural figure, which is the emergence of the head first and the second twin suspended or hanging by the umbilical cord.
Therefore, when you see these signs, it is appropriate to apply pressure on the woman's belly so that the fetus descends easily, because once the head emerges, the second twin should be delivered and cleaned of any excess matter with good hygiene.
But if the delivery is not natural and unacceptable, because when the fetus emerges with its body in front of its head and one foot or arm first, Or if the head and arm or the belly emerge first and it is quickly turned over with a presentation similar to unacceptable figures.
Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be knowledgeable and skillful in all these causes, and to avoid errors and deceptions.
And I will show you the complete figure of all those cases, and what signs are in each one so that they can be interpreted and understood.
When the fetus emerges with its head first due to natural labor, but it is heavy on the woman and makes delivery difficult, sometimes weakening her strength, then perform this technique or have the women do it themselves: apply fennel powder and warm oil to her perineum.
And then the midwife should insert her thumb between the woman's splayed fingers and press or use her fingernail to break up any excess moisture inside. And press on the woman's belly until she gives birth to the child.
But if it does not come out, then it is necessary for the woman to be massaged with powder made of fenugreek and chickpeas.
And then the midwife orders her to be massaged and makes her sniff a mixture of crushed herbs to make her sneeze, while covering her mouth and nose for an hour, because this will quickly cause the fetus to come out.
If both of the baby's arms came out first, then you must gently and gradually put them back in place. But if it does not obey the command to go back in, then place the woman on a cushion and raise her legs up, and then quickly shake the cushion on the ground while making sure that she does not fall during this movement.
But if the arms are not returned inside and the baby dies, then insert your fingers to extract the contents of the womb or attach the body to your hand with a cloth and pull it out gently. This will ensure that the fetus is expelled completely.
When the baby is positioned feet-first, you should first encourage its legs to come out fully, then gently turn it slightly, guiding the feet and legs into the correct position. After this, you can grab one of the baby's feet and slowly pull it out, gradually bringing the rest of the body along with it.
But if it has come out up to the hips, then you command it to come out, and make it sneeze with some crushed herbs, because it will be expelled if God so wishes.
If it is not expelled with what we have recommended, then you should slowly return the fetus back inside until it assumes a second natural position, because it will be expelled easily and gently at this point.
And if it is still forbidden with all that we have recommended, then take some powdered marshmallow root and slippery elm bark, and grind them well in a mortar to make a paste. Apply this paste to the woman's perineum, near the bottom of her belly. And then perform gentle massage with warm water on the hypochondria region until it becomes soft.
When you see that the lower parts of the baby have been relaxed, then perform fumigation with myrtle and gently place it on the baby. After fumigating for an hour, then place the baby on a cushion and make it sneeze by tickling its nose, then remove it from there and gently press the lower part of the woman's belly with light compression, because the fetus will soon be expelled.
When delivering a baby in transverse lie (one of its arms is raised above its head), it is important to first ensure that the mother's bladder is empty and to monitor the fetal heart rate. The midwife should then gently rotate the baby into a vertex or breech position, if possible, before proceeding with delivery. When delivering a fetus in transverse position with one of its arms up, the midwife should attempt to manipulate and guide the arm down towards the body. However, if reduction is not possible, the midwife can have the woman change her position by raising her hips or turning onto her side. This may help the fetus rotate into a more favorable position for delivery. It's important to be patient and gentle throughout this process to avoid causing harm to either the mother or the baby.
If the arm cannot be guided down, then have the woman lie on her side and shake her hips vigorously to try to dislodge the arm. Also, administer liquids and recommend taking demulcent medications.
When the delivery is complete, place the baby on a cushion and examine the arm that was up. Gently guide it back into its natural position, then have the mother take deep breaths and push again to help expel any remaining placenta or membranes.
When delivering a baby in the transverse position, with its arms and chest facing the mother's right or left side, the midwife should first attempt to manually rotate the fetus into a vertex or occiput anterior position. If this is not possible, the midwife can consider using forceps or vacuum extraction to assist in the delivery. However, these methods carry risks and should only be used by experienced medical professionals. In some cases, a cesarean section may be necessary for the safety of both the mother and the baby. It's important to carefully assess each individual situation and make decisions based on the best available evidence and expert guidance. The midwife should gently hold onto the baby's hand and slowly rotate it until it is in a better position for delivery, making sure to do so with ease.
When the baby is positioned correctly and gently guided out, then pause to apply a mixture of oil and emollients to the perineum to ease any discomfort or pain.
When the baby is delivered, gently guide it to lie on its side and place it on a cushion. Command the mother to push slowly and steadily. Once she has pushed, perform gentle massage on her belly while commanding her to incline to her right side. Apply pressure to her belly and make her sneeze with crushed herbs. The delivery of a prepared fetus lying on its side involves several steps. First, the midwife should ensure that the mother is in a comfortable position, usually on her side, with her lower leg supported and her upper leg slightly flexed. The midwife can then help guide the baby's shoulders and hips out, one at a time, using gentle traction and rotating movements.
When the baby comes out with difficulty from the mother's body in this way, consider that it may be necessary to manually extract any remaining membranes or fluids by using your fingernail to gently puncture and drain them.
If the fetus is suspended by its face and neck, then insert your finger into the umbilical cord to prevent it from being constricted and causing harm to the baby.
And apply pressure to the wound on the inside until the second one that is needed is stopped, and tell the woman to compress herself several times, and let the contents come out easily if God wills it.
The exit of twins or many fetuses. Know that twins are often born from many breeches, and sometimes three or four are born, but this is rare and happens late; but it is due to natural causes and not alive.
And it tells of those that are multiplied, a second pair, and they are separated by the hip, distinguishing between the ligament in the navel of each of them; and some of them are expelled with an easy natural birth, as is one fetus through gentle ejection, and others are expelled with difficult ejection, as we have mentioned.

On extracting the fetus when it is dead.
When you treat a dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medicine and it is not easily expelled, then you are forced to use manual operation with your hand. Therefore, it is important that you consider whether the woman is of strong constitution and does not have any of the conditions for which there is fear of losing her life.
Therefore, it is necessary for the woman to be positioned on her back with her buttocks raised and her head lowered, and her hips should be elevated.
The minister should hold the patient from two sides or have them tied to the bed, so that their body does not extend during the extraction of the stone.
Then moisten the mouth of the wound with warm oil and marshmallow mucilage, along with mucilage of althea and fenugreek seeds.
Then have the midwife apply those oils and mucilages to her hand and insert it into the wound with ease, and then carefully place her hand over the stone so that her fingers can close around it.[^1](#note-1)
And then place yourself in a convenient position: at this point, you should consider whether the stone is ready to come out by itself, and then insert your fingers either into the urethra or into the opening of the bladder, or into the mouth, or into the palate, or under the chin, or in the foramen caecum (a small depression at the base of the skull), or in the area near the ribs, or below the hypochondrium.
But if the stone is ready to come out through the urethra, then position yourself either at the anus or in the middle of the back.[^2](#note-2)
And it is necessary to insert the fingers of your right hand with the curve facing upwards into the space between the index and middle finger of your left hand, and carefully insert them into one of the openings mentioned earlier, until you reach the source of the problem (i.e., the stone).
Then place another finger or the third one if necessary alongside it to ensure that there is traction rather than extension of the urethra alone.
But be careful not to injure the surrounding tissue, just as is done in tooth extraction.
And in this procedure, it is important to keep the extension gentle and not force any part of the body that resists. If some parts are retained, then have the midwife apply her oiled fingers to them gently and carefully manipulate them until they come out easily.[^3](#note-3)
Therefore, if the stone is too large to come out through the opening, then insert your fingers into another part of the body that is wider and repeat this process until the entire stone has been removed.
But if the hand is unable to move past the other due to its constriction, then wrap a cloth around it and pull it out gently until it has been completely removed, inserting it either into the wrist joint or the armpit.
And you should do the same for the other hand and both feet if necessary.
But if the head of the stone is large or it becomes stuck during removal, or if water has accumulated around it, then insert a blunt instrument (such as a spoon) between the index and middle fingers and break open the stone, or use an instrument called "alundat" to remove it. The design of this instrument will be described in the following section.
Similarly, if the stone is naturally large and cannot be removed with ease, then insert it into a bladder or use an "alundat" as mentioned earlier, and remove the surrounding bones using forceps.
But if the head of the stone has come out but is stuck in the urethra, then it should be cut open to release the fluid that has accumulated in the bladder.[^4](#note-4)
But if it is not complicated or difficult to remove, then you should insert your fingers and remove the stone as soon as possible.
If there is an abscess or fluid accumulation in the lower abdomen, then you should puncture it to release the fluid that has accumulated inside.[^5](#note-5)
But if the stone is in its normal position in the bladder, then the traction required to remove it should be light and the direction of movement should be towards the opening of the urethra.
But if the stone is stuck between the abdomen and the pubic bone, then you should remove it with a cloth that you have wrapped around your hand, and make an incision in the abdomen and pubic region to release any accumulated fluid.[^6](#note-6)
But if other members are obstructed and the stone turns back towards the bladder, then have the midwife insert her left hand into the abdomen to feel for the stone and guide it towards the opening of the urethra. Then insert one or two fingers into the urethra and gently pull the stone out with them.[^7](#note-7)
But if the opening of the urethra is obstructed by an abscess or swelling caused by inflammation, then it should not be forcefully opened with a probe. Instead, warm compresses made from oils and fatty substances should be applied to reduce swelling and promote healing.[^8](#note-8) And administer poultices, and follow up with the patient using hydrating and softening treatments.
But if the stone is located on the side of the body, then it should be punctured if possible, and medication for a living stone should be administered as previously mentioned.
But if that is not possible, then insert forceps and extract it.
And it is necessary to make sure that no cause remains inside the bladder.
And once you have completed your entire procedure, then administer the treatment we have discussed for abscesses that occur around the urethral opening.
And if bleeding occurs, then use styptic waters and administer other treatments.
And I have seen a woman in whose belly was a dead stone, and over that fire another one became engorged, and the other stone died as well. It happened to a man who had an abscess in his navel for a long time, and it became so swollen that it burst open, and he began to emit pus from his arm.
I was called to care for him, and have treated him for a long time, but the wound has not healed.

On the treatment of fistulae that develop in the perineal area:
The fistulas that occur in the lower part of the body are knotty and large, which happen near the buttocks on the outside or in the groin area.

And the way to recognize a penetrating or non-penetrating fistula into the anus is by inserting your finger into the anus and gently probing with a thin piece of lead or iron in the fistula if there is no tortuousity (twisting).

But if it has penetrated into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and causes pain in the surrounding area, then a sign of this is that you can feel the probe entering it without any twisting into the bone, and experiencing pain in the surrounding area; and there will always be pus coming from it; and no medicine will work on it, nor will it heal with ointment.

The method of stitching up hemorrhoids where blood flows through the incision:
Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they protrude from the anus like charcoal, or they resemble clusters of grapes. And some are small and others are large, with blood constantly flowing from them and they are many, located outside the anus, at its edges.
However, those that are outside the anus are of two types based on the amount of moisture they contain: one type produces watery fluid or a small amount of blood with continuous flow and is the same color as the skin.
And the treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to sit on a stool and apply pressure until the anus protrudes and the hemorrhoids become visible. Then you should use forceps or your fingernails to make an incision along the edges of those hemorrhoids.
But if the forceps cannot hold onto those due to their moisture and softness, then take some rough fabric or cotton or a woolen cloth and pull them out with your fingers. Then make an incision along their edges and sprinkle some powdered cautery agents over them instead of using actual cauterization; or use cauterization as described in the chapter on cauterization. And then treat them with the same treatment until they are healed.
And if the anus does not protrude as required, then use a clyster to irrigate the patient with a small bite, and wash it with water that has been used in the anus to facilitate easy and gentle evacuation when the patient bears down.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then their cause is minor and you can simply use your fingernail or forceps to make an incision in them and then treat them with the same method until they heal.
And if you find an incision, then it is necessary to suture the hemorrhoids in the following manner: take some thread wrapped with a probe and insert it into a needle, then use the needle to pull the hemorrhoids up towards the edges, and push the needle through the edge of the other side. Then wrap the two ends of the thread around the lower part of the needle, transversely, and pull the hemorrhoid tight with strong tension, and then release the probe and remove the needle.
Do this for all of them, leaving one open and not stitching it up, so that excess blood can flow out from it.
And then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate over the anus, and let it rest on the area while instructing the patient to rest. And leave it in place until it comes out on its own. When that happens, treat the area with ointment or other methods until it heals.
And when they are old and do not respond to treatment, then it is necessary to make incisions in them using the tip of a spatula or your fingernail until they become moist and the hardened scab on top is removed, which prevents healing; and then treat them until they heal.
Then you should use more aggressive incisions, going deeper until there is significant bleeding and the area becomes scabbed over; then treat them until they heal.

Of treatment of plagues.
I have already said in the division of the treatment for plagues what was necessary for the book, and now I say this: the cure for that with my advice and with medications as appropriate.
Therefore, I say that plagues are differentiated according to what they are caused by and where they occur on the body.
And the causes by which plagues are often made include: stone throwing, knife or sword wounding, spear thrusting, staff or arrow shooting, and similar causes from many other sources.
But the plagues that occur on parts of the body include those such as a plague that affects the head, neck, chest, abdomen, thighs, and similar locations on the limbs.
And I am now recommending the treatment for some plagues so that you may apply this reasoning and rule to other plagues as well.
And I will begin with the simple plagues of the head, for the memory of the compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to stone throwing or something similar, and the skull has only been penetrated and it is a large wound and you fear an abscess may form, then quickly make an incision using the cephalic vein and do not delay. And extract from the wound as much blood as possible according to its capacity, unless there is some other reason preventing venesection, especially if little blood has come out from the wound itself.
And let the incision be on the opposite side of the affected area; and take care that the patient avoids replenishment, wine, and heavy foods.
But if some reason prevents you from making the incision, then lessen the patient's food and do not approach meat or wine.
And place over the wound if an abscess has formed, apply a piece of cloth soaked in oil or wine that has been steeped with styptic substances.
But if there is no danger of an abscess forming, then place over the wound, if it is fresh and still bleeding, a small amount of the powder that I will recommend next.
But if the air has already changed, then place various ointments on it until it heals.
But if the plague is large or caused by knife wounds and others like it, and the edges of the wound are not approximated with stitches as I will recommend in the chapter on sutures, then approximate them using suture according to my recommendation.
But if the plague has exposed the bone and is not a retention but only a small suspension, then incise it and cure the wound with medicines, restoring the flesh in place of the skull, and order the patient to abstain from foods that are heavy and cause coagulation until it heals.
And if you find putrefaction in the skull that does not adhere to the bone, then you should cut away all of it and remove it, and then cure it.
But if there is an artery or vein in these plagues from which blood can flow, and it has not been cut by medicines, then you should look for the artery, and if you find it uncut, then you should cut it with a scalpel or tie it off. And if necessity demands that what we have said is insufficient, then cauterize until the blood flow stops.
But if these plagues are simple and small, then their cause is light, so that you should powder over them this powder before the air changes around them, in order to consolidate them first before the air changes.
And the method for making the powder is this: take one part of divided oil, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of uncooked caustic substance; grind everything to a fine powder and fill the wound with it, then constrict it well with a tight bandage until it sticks to it, and let it coagulate with blood.
And then strengthen it above with stitches and leave it alone until it is not abscessed, for the medicine will not be effective until the wound heals completely.
And sometimes do only this cautery when you do not have oil and dragon's blood at hand.
And perform this method of treatment in large plagues when it is necessary to place it on them and constrict them, and only for recent wounds that are still bleeding, which the air has not yet altered.
But if the air has already altered them, especially in the summertime, then this method of powder is not suitable for their treatment. Instead, cure those wounds as I have previously described by applying various ointments or using a mixture made from barley flour, water, and honey to create a paste that can be applied to the wound until it heals completely.
But if a fracture occurs in the bone with a small wound, then you should extract it using gentle traction.
And I have already described the treatment for fractures of the skull in what is poisonous.
Of wounds to the neck.
But if a wound occurs in the neck, then it is not different in treatment from wounds to the head when they are simple.
But if the nerves of the neck are cut or an artery, if it is nerves, do not place anything in the wound, but rather avoid treatment with things that cause strong coagulation, such as cauterization with iron and similar substances, because they constrict nerves and cause contraction. And do not place any cause of cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold and its continuation is with the brain, which is the source of all members.
And if it is treated with light medicines, such as gentle washes with warm water, sometimes infused in rose oil or unscented oil, and incense when washed with warm water and other mild remedies according to this method, and moisturize with a warm compress.

On the treatment of abscesses and fistulas. (The title for the following text)
Know that any wound or abscess that becomes old and chronic, turns into an ulcer that does not consolidate and constantly drains pus, is universally called a fistula, and we call it "azuchem" in our language.
And in truth, a fistula is a hardened nodule that is white and painless, with a cavity similar to the cavity of a bird's feather quill, and for this reason it is called "azuchem" which means "razor quill."
And the fistula is a moist wound in humans, which constantly drains pus; and the moisture can be easily removed within a few hours. And sometimes this moisture is abundant, and it can be scanty, thick, or thin.
I have already explained all those causes and their signs and treatment with medicines in the division (of wounds).
And so, I need to tell you about the treatment of fistula which is done through surgery with hands.
Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body, and some of them reach large veins, arteries, nerves, the diaphragm, intestines, bladder, ribs, or spine, while others are close to major organs or joints such as those between the hand and arm or foot.
And therefore, this type of fistula, which is caused in this way, falls under the category of difficult-to-heal diseases and does not respond to treatment, and dealing with it requires hard work and ignorance (lack of knowledge).
If the depth of a particular fistula does not reach the locations that have been mentioned, and you hope for its healing, trust in its treatment and want to understand it better, then take an iron or steel probe and carefully examine the fistula. If it follows a straight path, then insert the probe into it.
But if the fistula is twisted, then examine it with a thin lead probe, as lead with its lightness of form can bend according to the twists and turns.
And if the fistula is hidden or obscured by many obstacles, it will not be possible for you to examine it with a probe.
In this case, clean the openings of the fistula with enema irrigation, as the liquid you use for cleaning will flow through other openings and remove the blockages.
Then examine it carefully, in any way that is possible for you to understand if there is a bone or nerve present, and whether the cavity of the fistula is deep or shallow. With all your strength, knowledge, questioning, and examination of the patient, determine the cause of the pain by pressing on the area with your hand and looking for signs and causes similar to those found in abscesses.
After considering all the causes and examining them carefully, then proceed to treatment based on your judgment: consider whether it is a superficial fistula near a healthy area or far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or one of the places I have mentioned.
Dry up the fistula as I have previously described in its narration, remove any material that has accumulated in it, such as corrupted flesh or matter coming out of the opening, and treat the wound until it heals completely.
But if the fistula is deeply located and follows a straight path, then you must incise it as much as possible with a probe, remove all the corrupted flesh from it, and apply hot compresses wrapped in sharp medicines inside its cavity which you have compressed with an iron instrument.
And do this several times until the sharp medicine corrodes all the dead tissue in the cavity of the fistula, removing the corruption.
Then restore it with unguents that promote healthy flesh growth until it heals completely.
But if it is not healed by this method, then you should cauterize the area as we have recommended.
But if you are certain that the cause of fistula is bone, then examine and dry it up as we have recommended, unless there is a reason to prohibit it due to an injury in vein, nerve or a major organ as we have mentioned before.
But if the bone is exposed and there is corruption or blackness in it, then cut around the area of the corruption until all of it has been removed, and then treat the wound with appropriate remedies until it heals completely.
But if it is not healed and continues to drain pus as before, then know that you have not yet completely removed the corruption. In this case, re-examine and clean the wound carefully and thoroughly, removing all remaining corruption with great care, and then restore it using appropriate remedies.
